Vienot, a staunch supporter of the League of Nations Covenant, will meet with Foreign Office advisor Strang, and it is possible that he will also call on Foreign Secretary Eden. In addition, Major Attlee, the leader of the British Labour Party opposition, is also scheduled to travel to Paris at the end of this week to hold talks with leaders of the French Socialist Party. The British Labour Party's attitude towards the sanctions issue will be determined as a result of Attlee's trip. Political figures here say that these semi-official talks between figures in and out of power in Britain and France will have an important impact on the League of Nations' policy towards Italy. (Havas Dispatch, 7th)

(Lisbon) The 90th regular session of the League of Nations Council, scheduled to convene on the 11th of this month, was departed from last night by Foreign Minister Monteiro and Vasconcelos, the Portuguese representative to the League of Nations (also Chairman of the League of Nations Assembly Sanctions Adjustment Committee and the Committee of Eighteen), via Paris to attend the meeting in Geneva. (Havas Dispatch, 6th)

British House of Lords Discusses the Issue of League of Nations Reform 34

Strong Support for Amending the Covenant

(London) The House of Lords met today to discuss the reorganization of the League of Nations. Liberal Party member Lord Lothian delivered a speech, stating, "In my view, it is not the concept of the League of Nations that has failed, but rather the principles enshrined in Articles 10 and 16 of the Covenant. These principles state that whenever there is an attempt to forcibly change the existing system anywhere, the member states of the League of Nations have an obligation to suppress it. This obligation is universal and automatic in nature, and it cannot be avoided. To be truly effective, it must involve war. This has been clearly demonstrated by recent experience. We are neither able nor willing to fulfill such an unlimited obligation. If we can state as soon as possible our determination not to fulfill this kind of obligation, we can quickly break free from the current situation and restore the past, allowing all issues concerning true world peace to be dealt with through diplomatic channels." Lord Lothian then cited several letters from American figures published in British newspapers to support his argument. The letters stated that if Articles 10 and 16 of the League of Nations Covenant could be abandoned, then the United States' view of the League of Nations could change significantly. Labour Party leader Lord Ponsonby then, in his personal capacity, asked the government whether it was prepared to submit to the League of Nations a proposal for reforming the collective security mechanism, and stated that he advocated adding the following provision to Article 18 of the Covenant: "The League of Nations should organize a special body to review all treaties registered by the Secretariat every two years, to determine whether they should be confirmed, amended, or suspended."

Note: Article 10 of the League of Nations Covenant states: "The Members of the League undertake to respect and preserve as against external aggression the territorial integrity and existing political independence of all Members of the League. In case of any such aggression or in case of any threat or danger of such aggression the Council shall advise upon the means by which this obligation shall be fulfilled."

Article 16 states: "Should any Member of the League resort to war in disregard of its covenants under Articles 12, 13 or 15, it shall ipso facto be deemed to have committed an act of war against all other Members of the League, which hereby undertake immediately to subject it to the severance of all trade or financial relations, the prohibition of all intercourse between their nationals and the nationals of the covenant-breaking State, and the prevention of all financial, commercial or personal intercourse between the nationals of the covenant-breaking State and the nationals of any other State, whether a Member of the League or not. It shall be the duty of the Council in such case to recommend to the several Governments concerned what effective military, naval or air force the Members of the League shall severally contribute to the armed forces to be used to protect the covenants of the League. The Members of the League agree, further, that they will mutually support one another in the financial and economic measures which are taken under this Article, in order to minimize the loss and inconvenience resulting therefrom, and that they will mutually support one another in resisting any special measures aimed at one of their number by the covenant-breaking State, and that they will take the necessary steps to afford passage through their territory to the forces of any of the Members of the League which are co-operating to protect the covenants of the League. Any Member of the League which has violated any covenant of the League may be declared to be no longer a Member of the League by a vote of the Council concurred in by the Representatives of all the other Members of the League represented thereon."

Article 18 states: "Every treaty or international engagement entered into hereafter by any Member of the League shall be forthwith registered with the Secretariat and shall as soon as possible be published by it. No such treaty or international engagement shall be binding until so registered." (Havas Dispatch, 7th)

(London) The Conservative Party's Foreign Affairs Committee recently met here to study in detail Britain's attitude towards the sanctions issue. After the meeting, a leader of the party told reporters that "the League of Nations' handling of the Italo-Ethiopian dispute has failed. Britain has nothing to be ashamed of, and the British government's policies have not lost the confidence of the public." He also said, "We believe that the issue of lifting sanctions must be approached with caution, and that the League of Nations must be reorganized if its actions are to be truly effective in the future. As for France, it must fully participate in any collective action, both now and in the future." According to Conservative Party sources, the majority party believes that lifting sanctions against Italy should be linked to amending the League of Nations Covenant. Sir Austen Chamberlain's statement in the House of Commons yesterday fully represents the views of this group. However, the current sanctions should be maintained until the new order in Abyssinia is established and a decision is made on amending the League of Nations Covenant. As for the amendment of the Covenant, the British government will seek the views of the Dominions, and it will be difficult to make proposals in the short term. (Havas Dispatch, 7th)

League of Nations Budget in Surplus 35

(Geneva) According to a communiqué issued by the League of Nations Secretariat, although the League of Nations is facing a political crisis, its financial situation is very good. The League of Nations' budget for this year is 28,279,000 Swiss francs (hereinafter abbreviated as such). As of April 30th, only 11,433,073 francs had been spent, of which the actual expenditure was only 8,30,245 francs, leaving a surplus of 3,129,828 francs, which is deposited in the bank. The arrears in membership fees from member states have decreased from 11.63% last year to 5.64%. In view of the surplus in this year's budget, the League of Nations Budget Supervisory Committee is considering three options: Reduce the membership fees of small countries; The surplus will be used as a public reserve fund; All remaining funds will be allocated to the Intelligence Division for publicity expenses, so that all countries have a deeper understanding of the League of Nations' activities. Which of the above three options will be adopted has not yet been decided. (Havas Dispatch, 7th)

The British Government's Memorandum in Response to Hitler's Proposal is Published - The List of Questions Contains Eleven Points, Requiring Supplementary Explanations in Polite Terms 41

(London) The British government's list of questions regarding the German memorandum of March 31st was published today in the form of a White Paper. In addition to the preface, it contains eleven key points in polite terms. On the one hand, it expresses satisfaction with certain points in the memorandum and the declarations issued by the German authorities, and on the other hand, it requests supplementary explanations or revisions to other points. Here is an excerpt from the original text:

Preface The British government sincerely hopes that all European countries can establish a truly lasting peace based on mutual recognition of independent rights and equal rights, and mutual respect for their accepted obligations. However, it is regrettable that the German government has failed to make a substantial contribution to restoring credibility as a major condition for extensive negotiations between Britain and Germany.

Main Text of the List of Questions The German government is currently willing to conclude honest treaties with the countries concerned.

The British government cannot agree with the German argument that the Treaty of Versailles and the various treaties arising from it should be abolished.

According to item 4 of the German memorandum, "There is a clear distinction between the German government and the German nation." The real question is whether the current Germany believes that the territorial status quo in European politics has reached a point where it can be recognized and respected. If there are those who are dissatisfied, can they conduct free negotiations with the countries concerned in the hope of reaching an agreement to correct them (i.e., not to correct them directly).

When German leader Hitler delivered a speech in the House of Representatives on May 21st last year, he proposed concluding a Western European aerial pact, but did not advocate the establishment of a regional air force limitation agreement to supplement the aerial pact, which the British government regrets.

The German government is willing to negotiate a 25-year mutual non-aggression pact with France and Belgium, with Britain and Italy as guarantor countries. The manner in which this pact should be formulated must be determined after negotiations have taken place. The British government has taken note of all of this.

The German government is prepared to negotiate mutual non-aggression pacts with neighboring countries in the Southeast and Northeast. The British government has also taken note of this and expresses satisfaction. However, the British government also wants to know whether these pacts can be supplemented by mutual assistance agreements.

"Since the German government has declared its eagerness to rejoin the League of Nations, the British government therefore believes that the bilateral mutual non-aggression pacts proposed by Germany can be integrated with the collective security obligations undertaken by member states of the League of Nations, and believes that these pacts can be used within the scope of the League of Nations Covenant without any difficulties."

It is good that the German government is willing to negotiate mutual non-aggression pacts with neighboring countries in the Southeast and Northeast. The British government firmly believes that if the so-called "neighboring countries in the Southeast and Northeast" can include the Soviet Union, Latvia, and Estonia in addition to the directly neighboring countries, the solution to various European problems will be greatly facilitated.

German leader Hitler said in a speech in the House of Representatives on May 21st last year that "Germany is always ready to sign international pacts to prevent interference in the internal affairs of other countries." The British government is now happy to reiterate this.

What about the international arbitration tribunal proposed by Germany? The British government hereby requests clarification and states that there is already a permanent international tribunal in The Hague.

Regarding the separation of the League of Nations Covenant from the Treaty of Versailles, what is the content? The British government sincerely hopes that the German government will provide additional explanations. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

(Berlin) It was learned here today that the list of questions submitted by British Ambassador to Germany Phipps to German Foreign Minister Neurath is intended to probe the true intentions of German leader Hitler on general issues. The list does not mention the colonial issue at all, because Britain is currently unwilling to discuss the restoration of Germany's lost territories, and hopes that Germany will be able to abide by international obligations in the future, respect the independence of Austria, and the legal status of Memel and Danzig Free City. (National Telegram, 7th)

Japanese House of Representatives Budget Debate: Military Spending Expansion Under Heavy Attack 46

Social Masses Party Leader Hisashi Aso Scathingly Criticizes the Military for Disregarding the People's Livelihoods

(Tokyo) At the Diet session on the 7th, Saito Takao of the Minseito Party questioned the military and the issue of constitutional politics, sparking a heated debate that made the atmosphere in the chamber tense. On the 8th, because the House of Peers was not holding a formal meeting, the center of political debate shifted to the House of Representatives. The House of Representatives convened its first general meeting on the budget at 9:00 AM and began the questioning. Ti, Wakamiya, Taketomi, and others successively expressed their opinions, discussing issues such as reforming the tax system, revitalizing finances, establishing local finances, and expanding industry and trade, pressing the government and scrutinizing its policies. The plenary session convened at 1:00 PM. In addition to speeches by Iwasaki, Muramatsu, and Miyoshi, Hisashi Aso, the leader of the Social Masses Party, which won 18 seats in the recent election and is the only opposition party, appeared on the stage for the first time to thoroughly criticize the current government's policies. He questioned the government's beliefs on issues such as finance, the economy, diplomacy, and military reduction. Therefore, today's meeting is sure to have a heated debate.

(Tokyo) The House of Representatives convened at 1:34 PM and continued with the questioning. First, Iwasaki Koji of the Seiyukai Party demanded that the authorities reflect on issues such as the abuses in the application of the constitution, the reform of the emergency situation, the irrational crackdowns by the police, and other violations of human rights. Prime Minister Hirota, Army Minister Terauchi, Interior Minister Shio, and Justice Minister Hayashi each gave simple answers. Regarding the issue of stabilizing the people's livelihood, Muramatsu Hisayoshi and Nagai Ryutaro of the "Minseito" Party questioned the Finance and Army Ministers. Furthermore, regarding the land tenant issue, they questioned the authorities. The Prime Minister, Finance Minister, Commerce Minister, Agriculture Minister, and Navy Minister each took the stand to answer. Subsequently, at 4:08 PM, Miyoshi Nobufusa of the Seiyukai Party questioned issues such as rural problems, debt consolidation, balanced burdens, and local financial allocations. The Prime Minister, Finance Minister, Interior Minister, Colonial Minister, Army Minister, and others each gave simple answers. Then, Hisashi Aso of the Shakai Taishuto Party delivered his maiden speech, attacking the Army Minister regarding the issue of stabilizing the people's livelihood and the military's sole focus on expanding the budget without regard for the people's safety. Regarding the diplomatic issue, he briefly stated:

The current Sino-Japanese relationship is truly very serious. However, the closest period of Sino-Japanese relations was rooted in the ideas of the Chinese Revolution. At that time, Chinese and Japanese revolutionaries were closely united. Later, with the development of the capitalism of the great powers, rifts appeared in Sino-Japanese relations, and there is no so-called guiding principle to this day.

He then advocated for adjusting Sino-Japanese relations and constructing "Manchukuo," establishing a kingdom based on benevolent rule without exploitation, and establishing an ideal guiding principle.

Foreign Minister Arita replied as follows:

Even during the Chinese Revolution, Sino-Japanese relations cannot be considered friendly. We should strive to adjust them in the future. The adjustment of relations with the Soviet Union also goes without saying, but we hope that the ideas of our people will develop in a healthy way, and we should strive for that.

At this point, Akira Kazami of the "Kokumin Domei" Party raised several questions, as follows:

Will a general tax be levied on the masses? If you tout economic diplomacy, it will be detrimental to the 400 million people of China. Are there any countermeasures for the agricultural panic in China?

Finance Minister Baba replied as follows:

I will not levy a general tax on the masses that threatens the people's livelihood.

Foreign Minister Arita replied as follows:

One way to help Chinese farmers is to export cheap Japanese goods to them, and on the other hand, to purchase cheap leather and other raw materials produced by Chinese farmers, hoping to cooperate and help each other.

Navy Minister Nagano and Army Minister Terauchi made some replies regarding military industry and military reduction for retired soldiers. The meeting adjourned at 7:28 PM. (Domei News Agency, 8th)

(Tokyo) The House of Representatives Budget Committee convened at 9:12 AM on the 8th. Prime Minister Hirota and all other cabinet members and committee members attended. First, Committee Chairman Kawasaki reported on the budget committee's schedule and other matters. Then, the additional budget for the 11th year was taken up as the topic, and questioning began.

The first questioner, Tei Kojiro (Minseito Party), rose and asked the three ministers of the Army, Navy, and Foreign Affairs, stating that it was inappropriate for diplomacy to be controlled by the three ministers in meetings.

Ministers Arita and Terauchi defended the possibility of such control. Tei then turned his attention to Prime Minister Hirota, saying that the people imagined that war was about to break out. He asked about the recent relations with Russia.

Prime Minister Hirota replied that regarding Japan's international situation, including its relations with Russia, the world also had doubts. However, he took office as prime minister because he was confident that he could overcome these problems.

Tei asked what the general outlook was for Army equipment preparation costs and Navy shipbuilding costs.

Army Minister Terauchi replied that the new expenses for the 11th year belonged to the basic matters under consideration by the military, and that expenses for expanding the garrison in Manchuria, aviation, and air defense were appropriate. The expenses for the 12th year and beyond are currently under study. Although the numbers cannot be clearly indicated at present, the Army budget will temporarily increase in the future. Navy Minister Nagano replied that the specific numbers for Navy shipbuilding expenses could not be clearly indicated except in a closed-door meeting.

After Tei finished questioning, Wakamiya Sadao (Seiyukai) rose. First, he requested the dissemination of diplomatic knowledge to the Prime Minister. Then, he asked about the content of the communications and propaganda policy, and further asked about his belief in so-called national reform and upholding constitutional politics.

Prime Minister Hirota replied that he also recognized the necessity of disseminating international knowledge to the people and that the government was preparing to expand and strengthen communications agencies and raise their level to the world standard. At this time, Uehara Seiichiro (Seiyukai) questioned the Prime Minister about the issues of parliamentary politics and constitutional operation, saying that the Prime Minister should not explicitly attribute the responsibility for social unrest to the parliament.

The Prime Minister clarified the reason why his statement did not have this meaning.

Wakamiya then asked that the government's proposed budget did not contain any ambition for national reform, which was a pity.

He then turned the topic to the issue of economic control, saying that the act of restricting the entire people for the elimination of a small portion of abuses should be approached with caution. He also said that there were too many government-appointed members on the various committees, which was not what people wanted. He asked what the Prime Minister's opinion was.

The Prime Minister replied that he would give it full consideration.

The meeting adjourned at 12:05 AM. (Domei News Agency, 8th)

The entire line is 1096 kilometers long, with 90 stations of varying sizes, and takes 43 and a half hours. After the official opening, it is planned to reduce the time to 36 hours. Measures for Penalties for Mixing Refined Salt with Huai Salt 62

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has stipulated measures for penalties for mixing and selling refined Huai salt. If any salt shop in the area where refined salt is allowed to be sold is found to be selling refined salt as Huai salt, it should be fined twice the difference in price between refined salt and Huai salt in the area, according to the amount of salt sold, to show strict enforcement. However, this mixing method is limited to the amount of salt that constitutes the mixing result, and the taxes have been fully paid. If there is any collusion or malpractice, it will still be investigated as smuggled salt. The income from the fines should be turned over to the public treasury. The regulations have been communicated to all salt affairs agencies for compliance. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Guangzhou: Another Counterfeit Currency Case Cracked 87

Five suspects arrested and sent to the Finance Department for interrogation. Counterfeit 50-cent notes sold for only 65% of their face value.

Since the province implemented currency reform, legal tender has been in high demand because silver is no longer in circulation. In addition to the provincial and municipal banks successively issuing new one-yuan and five-yuan notes to facilitate circulation, the provincial bank also printed a "50-cent" note through Xinhua Company in Hong Kong. The front features a blue print of the Pearl River Iron Bridge, and the back is ochre, with the face value of 50 cents written in Arabic numerals. Since its issuance, it has been easily counterfeited. Before long, a large number of counterfeit 50-cent notes were found on the market. The authorities became aware of the situation and, on one hand, announced that the provincial bank would recall the 50-cent notes, and on the other hand, sent detectives to investigate the source of the counterfeit currency. It was not until the 2nd of this month that a counterfeit currency trafficking organization was cracked. Initially, Hu, a field officer of the Agricultural Products Special Tax Bureau, discovered clues after more than a month of secret investigation. It was found that the 50-cent counterfeit notes printed by the criminals were sold at low prices, with each 100 yuan of counterfeit notes selling for only 65 yuan. Many unscrupulous merchants, taking advantage of the low price, purchased a large number and mixed them into the market. Hu persuaded a middleman, pretending to want to buy counterfeit notes for 400 yuan, and instructed the middleman to contact the sellers of the counterfeit notes. It was agreed that the deposit would be paid at the Xiangzhen Tea House in Ximen on the 2nd, and the counterfeit notes would be delivered at the Xuan Palace Hotel on Taiping South Road in the afternoon. Once the agreement was finalized, Hu immediately reported to the Agricultural Tax Bureau, which in turn reported to the Finance Department. On the same day, the Finance Department dispatched Commissioner Wu with a warrant, accompanied by Section Chief Lu and investigators Zhou and Lin of the Agricultural Tax Bureau, armed with firearms, to ambush the Xuan Palace Hotel. First, Hu, the field officer, accompanied the middleman to the Xiangzhen Tea House as scheduled to negotiate with the sellers of the counterfeit notes. After agreeing on the price, the sellers of the counterfeit notes arrived at the Xuan Palace Hotel with the counterfeit notes at around 3:00 PM in the afternoon. However, the criminals were very cunning, fearing they were being set up. First, they sent a person with a bamboo tube in his pocket, seemingly containing money, meaning that even if searched, there would be no evidence. If the person carrying the counterfeit currency arrived later, he could escape after hearing the news. Unexpectedly, the detectives turned the tables and treated the person who came to test the waters with kindness, without rashly searching him, so there was no commotion outside. Soon, the person carrying the counterfeit currency arrived, took out a bundle of counterfeit 50-cent notes from his pocket, saying that the total amount was only 150 yuan. The detective said it was not enough and asked him to bring more. The sellers of the counterfeit notes demanded 80 yuan before they would send more. Just as they were negotiating, a signal was given, and the Finance Department Commissioner and the Agricultural Tax Bureau investigators rushed in with guns, immediately capturing Wu Fa and two other sellers of counterfeit notes. They also dispatched detectives to Wu Fa's residence at No. 4, Penglai North Street, Guangxiao Branch, where they only found more than a dozen receipts for the sale of counterfeit notes, but no printing machines or other items were found. They also arrested a man named Chen at Wu's residence, who had more than 100 yuan of legal tender on him, claiming that he had come to buy counterfeit notes. Another man named Wu was also arrested. The above five suspects were transferred to the Finance Department's Preliminary Trial Office for interrogation on the same day. The counterfeit 50-cent notes that were seized were identical to the real ones in color and paper quality, and most ordinary people could not distinguish them. However, upon closer inspection, the numbers on the counterfeit notes all started with digits such as 1070000. The Finance Department is currently interrogating the seller of counterfeit notes, Wu Fa, to investigate the source in order to crack down on the counterfeit currency printing organization. (Evening of May 4th)

Municipal Progress in Fuzhou 88

Rivers - Streets - Tap Water

Fuzhou Correspondence: In the upper reaches of the Min River, every spring and summer, there are continuous rainstorms, and the creeks and floods surge, and the river flows overflow, flowing directly into Fuzhou. The river channels in the city are silted up, and the water volume cannot be discharged, so the low-lying areas become swamp lands. After the floods, the soil becomes humid, leading to the breeding of epidemics, which affects the society and the people. The current Provincial Capital Works Department, in order to prevent floods, in addition to actively dredging the river channels in various places to facilitate the flow of water, will also repair the rainwater gates outside the northwest of the city. If there is a rise in the upstream water level, the water gates will be lowered to kill the water momentum. At the same time, the roadbeds of low-lying areas such as the Huancheng Road will be raised to act as dams to block the water force and prevent the upstream water flow from rushing into the provincial capital. At the same time, it is also planned to demolish all the piers of the Xiaobao Bridge on Nantai and build a new straight-beam bridge to facilitate the flow of water. The construction of roads and the repair of fences are currently under construction. However, the demolition of the bridge cannot be carried out immediately due to limited funds. However, this measure is of great importance to the people's livelihood, and the department is working hard to plan and strive to achieve its completion in the short term. As for the streets of the city, they are all dirty and overflowing. The most prosperous areas are the South Main Road and Zhongting Street. However, the streets in these areas are not very wide, and in the event of a fire, it is easy to spread. It has also been decided to expand them. At present, business is sluggish, and the people's strength may not be sufficient. However, the opening of roads is to facilitate traffic throughout the city, and also to develop the city's commerce. The government and the people should tolerate temporary pain and support its success. Regarding this plan, the surveying work of each road has been completed, and it will be started when the business is restored. As for all the civil houses and shops on both sides of the road, they will be recovered in accordance with the land price and the assessed value in the future, so that the people will not suffer any losses. However, the amount of this land price is too large, and it is definitely not the government's responsibility. According to the current measures promulgated by the central government, in addition to the demolition of the houses, the value will be given back, and the cost of road construction in the area will be estimated. Road fees will be collected from the newly built shops on both sides, depending on the business situation, not exceeding 60%. In this way, neither the government nor the people will suffer any losses. After the old shops on the side of the road are demolished, the houses behind them will leap forward, and traffic and business will be greatly facilitated. It seems not too important to collect these few road fees. The department is currently carefully considering this collection method to ensure that the people are not troubled and the traffic is convenient. In addition, the Provincial Capital Tap Water Preparatory Office has decided to build the water plant on Longtan Mountain on the right bank of the Min River, and is planning the requisition of land and the relocation of obstacles on the ground. As for the materials and machinery of the water plant, the calculation has been completed, and the Construction Department has sent letters to the Shanghai Purchasing Committee, the Construction Committee, the Central Trust Bureau, and a certain company to inquire about the value. Bids will be submitted on June 1st, and the start-up fee is estimated at more than 1.7 million yuan. As soon as the bidding is ready, construction will begin. (May 6th)

Travels in Qinghai (Continued) 89

— Zhuang Xueben

(III) The Mongol Banner of Qunke Beach

Failure to go to Qaidam: The "Qaidam" basin occupies one-third of the area of Qinghai Province. It is close to Xinjiang and has a purely nomadic Mongol ethnicity. The climate is warm, and there are cultivated farmlands, but the desert land is sparsely populated, so few tourists and merchants go there. The political power has not yet extended there. The good wilderness is still a desolate white land. After returning to Xining from the Ta'er Temple, I harbored the ambition to invade this white land to investigate the Mongol ethnicity and geography, but there were more than a dozen horse stations between there and Xining. The road was all barren, so I had to bring my own tent. There was unrest on the road, so I had to bring guns, or have military escorts. It was not easy for someone empty-handed to come and go at will. At that time, I negotiated with the military headquarters, and they were very willing to send an adjutant who spoke Mongolian, two guards, and two riding horses to escort us. Therefore, we prepared all the necessary items for the road and waited. Soon, twelve days passed, and the adjutant in the military headquarters could not be sent out for a while. Most of them were on official business, and the remaining few could only speak Tibetan and not Mongolian. They insisted on staying a few more days.

On the morning of February 20th, we could not wait any longer. We went to Huangyuan to look for opportunities, or follow a large group of merchants. At eight o'clock in the morning, we hired a large car and left Xining City, heading west towards Huangyuan. The road was all paved. It had been sunny for a long time, and the dust was very heavy. Our tracheas were full of dust and sand brought up by the hooves of the mules in front. This ninety-li road was very long. It was not until after the sun went down at one o'clock that the two tired mules dragged us into a dark and dirty mule and horse shop. This is the East Pass of Huangyuan.

The next morning, we met the newly appointed County Chief Zhu and the Chamber of Commerce President in the county government. They showed concern about my going to Qaidam because it was the period of the lunar new year, and the large group of merchants had not yet started. If a few people went, it would be extremely difficult to defend themselves on the road, find lodging and food, and hire laborers and horses. Therefore, our hot hope was frustrated. Although I never wanted to give up the investigation of the Mongol ethnicity, after some consideration, I decided on the plan to go to Qunke Beach in northeastern Qinghai.

The scene of Huangyuan: We were delayed in Huangyuan for exactly one day. In the city, there were many Tibetans wandering on the street, wearing old sheepskin coats and holding a few newly peeled lamb skins, seeking to sell them, and there were also many Mongols coming and going, leading camels. This place is obviously a large commercial market. The transactions of Mongols and Tibetans in western Qinghai are concentrated here. The quantity of wool, lambskin, and medicinal materials exported every year is considerable. The total amount of wool alone is more than 2 million catties. This year, the price of wool in Tianjin is good, so the wool market is more active. The local market price is currently 15 yuan per hundred catties.

Huangyuan was formerly known as "Dangar." It was not until the second year of the Republic of China that it was changed to a county seat. It controls the throat of Mongol and Tibetan areas such as Qaidam and Yushu, so it is also very important in geographical terms. Now, west of Huangyuan, the number of Han and Hui residents gradually decreases and even disappears. People's lives have also regressed from agricultural society to nomadic society. People generally call the area west of Huangyuan "the outside."

The city is narrow and long, and the area is very small, half a mile east-west. The area of the entire county is very large, more than 4,300 square li, but it is still smaller compared to the area of other counties in the province. The terrain is 2,635 meters high, and the surrounding area is all flat land, facing the Bin of the Huangshui River. The land is fertile and produces crops, and the majestic poplars form sparse forests.

The residents in the city are divided into Han and Hui in ten places. The area around the East Pass is inhabited by Muslims. Most of the shops in the city are merchants from Shaanxi and Gansu. The traffic with the provincial capital is good, and cars can also travel on the main road. Postal and telephone services are also available. The highest schools in the county are the primary schools for boys and girls. In this important border area, education is backward and pitiful.

Eating in restaurants is very expensive. A plate of mutton costs 60 cents, and a plate of chicken costs 80 cents, but if you only eat rice and don't eat vegetables, the price is cheaper. A plate of sliced noodles or noodles costs only five cents, because it is the local people's custom to eat rice without eating vegetables often.

Strong wind blows down the horse: On the 22nd, we set off for "Qunke Beach." The county government sent a policeman and three district courier horses to escort us. Following the main road to the west, farmland and houses appeared in the poplar forest. Five li away, we reached the "Huangshui River." Here, we separated from the avenue to "Halakutu," turned north, and the farms of the Han people gradually became sparse. The mountain slopes on both sides were pressing towards the road.

The windy and sunny atmosphere also slowly turned into windy and gloomy weather. A burst of gusts of wind, from time to time mixed with sand and gravel, attacked our faces. The branches on the left and right were all roaring, and the air was filled with yellow dust. The surrounding scenery was all blurred.

Twenty li away, the Huangshui River flowed out of a steep mountain gorge. The river was frozen into two-foot-thick ice. Our horses stepped onto the slippery ice slope and went in. The oncoming wind blew more fiercely. The stone walls on both sides revealed jagged skeletons. Going in here is "Zasa Temple." We planned to rest in the temple for a while and drink a cup of tea.

Suddenly, a sharp sound came from under the stone wall, and a large vortex of sand and wind rose, sweeping past us. This was our first experience. Our faces were stinging from being hit by gravel, our respirators were blocked, and our eyes were forced to close tightly. At this time, I leaned on the horse's back and tightened my legs, fearing that the horse would slip and fall. The sensible animal also lowered its head and stood still and could no longer move. At this time, we quietly waited for the storm to pass. After a minute, the roaring sound in our ears gradually died down. The wind had passed, and when we opened our eyes, we were blinded by yellow sand. We found that one of our old horses carrying luggage had been blown down on the ice. We were busy lifting it up. Fortunately, it was not injured, so we continued to move forward, carefully and quickly passing through the mouth of the gorge, preventing the second violent storm from striking.

Inside the mountain gorge, the place was much more open. The mountain dwellings were connected into a row of very small villages. On the mountain on the south bank of the river, there was a clump of green mountain forest, hiding many houses. That was the "Zacang Temple." We crossed the bridge to visit. In a continuous reception room, we drank a cup of tea and ate a piece of pancake. The Kanbu (abbot) in the temple also led us to visit the scripture hall and the Great Hall.

We wanted to travel another thirty li, so we hurriedly climbed back onto our horses and went north along the foothills. The fierce wind and sand still attacked from time to time. I lay on the horse's back and urged it forward, but the horse was also an animal, and it could not resist the natural violence, so its movements were very slow. When the wind was strong, it just stood still. In half an hour, we only traveled three li. Here, there were farmers' villages along the road. The slope was rising, and the altitude reached 2,840 meters. The wind was blowing harder and harder, and the oncoming sand and stones hit us so hard that we could not open our eyes. The dirt on our faces was like the bottom of a pot. We asked the police to find a place to stay. Fortunately, a Mongol Zhangjing (township head) invited us to his home. The Zhangjing's name was "Cao Getili." He was a Mongolian who could speak Chinese and was enlightened. Talking about everything in the evening was not lonely.

The eighth nomadic land: Early one morning, we left the village of "Baiyangxia," and the sincere and friendly Old Master Cao rode his horse and personally sent us twenty li to the north. That day, we were still going upstream along the Huang River. The river was two-thirds narrower than downstream of Huangyuan. There were still Mongols cultivating on the slopes on both sides, but the population was gradually decreasing. The cold was severe in the morning, but the wind was slight.

Twenty-five li later, the horse changed to the east bank of the Huang River and went forward. The mountains gradually spread to both sides, and the slopes became much gentler. The remaining yellow and withered grass covered the wilderness, showing the earth's dryness and lifelessness. The future was vast, and we could not see a single earthen house or a pedestrian. There was no formal road here either. Any mountain slope that the horses' hooves trampled on could be considered a road.

Near noon, the wind started to blow again. Because this place is very close to the sea, there is a strong wind every afternoon. A mountain ditch led us in, and we climbed a slope of thirty-five degrees again. From here, we saw a group of hundreds of cattle and sheep grazing on the meadow in front. When our line passed in front of them, they all tilted their heads and admired the style of our group of visiting travelers.

The cattle inside were all yaks with fur hanging down to the ground, and the sheep were all large-tailed sheep. It was the cold winter, so the down on the cattle and sheep was even more fluffy and cute. The dry grass had all withered and stuck to the ground, but they were still chewing with taste, so the water had not seen much weight loss, because they were the masters of the wilderness.

Two or three li ahead, there were a few black tents (this was the first time I saw the tents of nomads). The big shaggy dogs were already barking when they saw the silhouettes of people in the distance. The mountain road went around the back of the tent. The barking of the shaggy dogs awakened the owners of several black tents to come out and see what was going on.

Songjiang: Finance Department Commissioner Inspects Tax Collection 90

Yesterday, the Finance Department dispatched Commissioner Gu Xingqing to the Songjiang County Office. Accompanied by Secretary Shen Zhinzhi, he went to the local donation and tax collection office and the deed tax office to inspect them, examining the various books in detail. He left the county after an hour. It is rumored that he plans to stay for two more days.

The Commissioner's Office Will Hold a Construction Meeting 91

Yesterday, the Administrative Inspector Commissioner's Office convened a construction meeting of the counties under its third district. The heads of the construction departments of each county attended. Commissioner Wang presided over the meeting. As a result of the talks, after reporting the construction of roads in each county, the funds were planned, and roads and telephone networks were built. After returning to the counties, the heads of the construction departments of each county will implement them separately.

Planned Reconstruction of Taoxing Bridge 92

The Taoxing Bridge, located outside the west gate of the city, has high stone steps, causing considerable inconvenience to pedestrians and posing difficulties for fire fighting. Local enthusiasts, including Yang Bingwen, have initiated the construction of a flat bridge made of cement and steel, requiring funds of over one thousand gold yuan. The groundbreaking ceremony is scheduled for the ninth of this month. Besides applying to the county government for an allocation from the construction budget, the initiators will solicit donations to cover any shortfall in funds.

Establishment of Kunshan Commercial Arbitration Office 93

Disputes frequently arise among businesses in this county. During the recent re-election of the Chamber of Commerce, members proposed organizing a Commercial Arbitration Office to mediate disputes. It was officially established on the seventh of this month, with Xu Jiyang elected as the director.

Taicang Road Workers Robbing on the Road 94

Due to continuous rainfall in recent days, the Kunshan-Taicang motor road has become uneven, causing great inconvenience for vehicles. Road workers are currently repairing it in sections. However, these workers are constantly taking advantage of their position to cause trouble, committing adultery, robbery, and all sorts of crimes. Nearby villagers have suffered greatly. Around 2 PM on the seventh, Lin Ruifen, a concubine of Wu Zijin, a resident of Zhendong Township, was traveling from Taicang to the township with her adopted daughter, Meiya, when they were suddenly stopped near Wutang Bridge by road workers. One of them, Li Yusheng from Liyang, grabbed Lin by the waist and held her. Another worker robbed her of a diamond ring worth over five hundred yuan. Meiya, witnessing this, ran to tell her father. Wu Zijin went and bravely captured Li Jinsheng, handing him over to the police station at the West Gate for transfer to the Public Security Bureau for judicial proceedings. It is reported that other workers are making threatening noises and are unwilling to submit.

Suzhou Panic Over the Implementation of Public Prostitution 95

Public prostitution has been implemented in Suzhou. The Public Security Bureau is being very strict in cracking down on private prostitution and prohibiting gambling in brothels. Public and private prostitutes are not allowed to stay or hide in hotels. Hotels found to be violating this regulation will have their licenses revoked. As a result, hotels are in a state of panic because it is difficult to distinguish prostitutes from respectable women. The Hotel Industry Association has petitioned the county government for relief. The county government issued a reply yesterday stating: "We are aware of your petition. Is it really that difficult to distinguish people from Qilou (brothels)? Why is it that hotel staff can procure prostitutes whenever a guest requests one? These women have their own nests. Unless a guest keeps them, why would they be alone and lonely in a hotel, keeping watch alone at night? As for visiting relatives and friends, everyone is free to do so, and the association cannot prohibit it. However, the drinker's heart is not in the wine. If they are using this as an excuse to engage in prostitution and entice customers, should the hotel not be responsible for prohibiting it? In the past, hotel staff considered introducing prostitutes to guests as a source of profit, and the responsible personnel of each member hotel did not prohibit it in order to increase business, damaging public morals and harming travelers. This has been a long-standing practice. Now that the government has explicitly ordered a crackdown, the members of the association are not only failing to comply with the instructions but are daring to use sophistry to try to evade responsibility, which is extremely ignorant of the greater good. Your request is denied." Furthermore, a group of prostitutes (from high-end brothels) at the Cangxian Villa were caught gambling by the Public Security Bureau, and their patrons, including Wang Mingdong, were arrested. As a result, the high-end brothels are in a state of panic, believing that such restrictions by the Public Security Bureau will make it impossible to conduct business. They are also requesting leniency from the authorities. If their requests are not met, they are determined to surrender their licenses and cease operations.

Silk Industry to Petition the Government 96

The Wu County yarn and satin shops, iron weaving factories, and silk industry associations, noting that Wu County is a silk-producing area, with over 30,000 silk weavers ten years ago and all products sold to the Northeast provinces and the South Sea Islands, have seen a sharp decline in Suzhou yarn and satin sales due to the prevalence of rayon and the dumping of foreign goods. Now there are only over 2,000 silk weavers, and silk weaving factories are in danger. With recent rampant smuggling in North China, rayon is being imported in large quantities, causing public anxiety and further lowering the prices of silk products. Therefore, leaders of these industries have decided to petition the government to quickly establish a rayon factory to reduce costs and make silk products easier to sell, thereby maintaining the livelihoods of workers and regaining control. As for the issue of saving natural silk, it is reported by those in the industry that the authorities of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have jointly discussed uniting large and small silk factories in both provinces to organize a Jiangsu-Zhejiang Joint Silk Reeling Company, to increase quality, reduce production costs, and facilitate sales abroad. If this plan can be realized, the silk industry of Wu County may have a hope of revival.

Jiading Stray Bullet from Target Practice Accidentally Injures Farmer 97

The city's security squadron held live ammunition target practice on the seventh, at the old clock tower in the city. Red flags were erected and warnings were posted around the shooting range in the morning. Starting at 1 PM, around 3 PM, a stray bullet flew out from the city wall and landed behind the Zizong Temple, more than two miles away from the city. It struck Zhu Hongsheng, a farmer working in the field, piercing his right arm and chest, causing him to faint and bleed profusely. He was immediately sent to Cunren Hospital in the city for treatment.

Wuxi North China Yarn Factory Operators Visit 98

The North China Yarn Industry Delegation, organized by Dong Heng and Chen Peiqi of the Weihui Hua Yarn Factory, Zai Wenzhu of the Shanxi Shijiazhuang Daxing Yarn Factory, Liu Chijun of the Yuci Jinhua Yarn Factory, Yan Qingxiang and Li Nailv of the Henan Zhengzhou Yufeng Yarn Factory, and Zhang Minggang, president of the Bank of China in Taiyuan, Shanxi, consisted of more than 20 people. They came to Suzhou to visit various industrial factories, such as silk, yarn, and flour mills. After a brief stay in Shanghai, they were accompanied by Zhai Xingeng of the China Merchants' Yarn Factory Association to Suzhou to visit the Sulun Yarn Factory. The day before yesterday, they came to Wuxi and stayed at the New World Hotel. Subsequently, representatives from the Cotton Textile Industry Association accompanied them to visit the Lixin Qingfeng Textile Dyeing and Finishing Factory and toured Huishan Mountain. Jiang Shangda and Liu Guojun from the Changzhou textile industry also came to Wuxi to meet them. In the evening, Wuxi textile industry leaders Cai Qiansan and Cheng Jingtang hosted them at the Yingbin Restaurant. Yesterday morning, they visited the Shenxin No. 3 Factory and toured Taihu Lake. This morning, Jiang Da and others accompanied them to Changzhou to visit the Dacheng Minfeng Yarn Factory. They will return to Shanghai and then head north tomorrow.

Changshu Rioters Sent to Wuxi for Trial 99

In Shazhou City, the seventh district of Changshu County, rioters recently obstructed river work, destroyed the township head's residence, seized official documents, and assaulted police officers resisting arrest. The county dispatched a police squad to suppress the riot. The Wuxi District Administrative Commissioner sent staff member Zhang Yuzhong to investigate and ordered the county magistrate to resolve the situation quickly. Twelve people, including Xu Dafu, Ju Jinhuang, and Xiao Song, who led the riot, have been arrested and sent to the Wuxi District Security Command for military trial. After questioning by Judge Li, they were ordered to be detained pending further investigation.

Pharmacy Apprentice Falls from Building and Commits Suicide 100

Pang Ruichun, an apprentice at Zhang Renzhi Tang Pharmacy, located west of the Jieguan Pavilion in Beitang, this city, which is run by traditional Chinese medicine practitioner Zhang Tianan, was 18 years old and from Gushan, Jiangyin. He had completed his apprenticeship this year. On the afternoon of the fifth of this month, Ruichun went upstairs to fetch medicinal materials, accidentally lost his footing, and fell to the ground. He immediately lost consciousness. The pharmacy did not call a doctor for treatment and left him moaning in bed. Ruichun's brother, Ruibiao, learned of this and transported him to Puren Hospital for treatment. However, when the cart reached Mianjin Bridge at the South Gate, he had already died from his injuries. The deceased's face was blue and purple, and his abdomen was swollen, which was quite strange. The body was temporarily placed in the Yaohuang Temple on Sanhuang Street. Mao Zijun, the head of the fourth district in the north, reported to the local court requesting an autopsy. After receiving the report, the prosecutor, accompanied by Shen, a coroner, and judicial police chief Zhu Wanyuan, went to perform the autopsy at 10 AM yesterday (the 8th). The autopsy revealed several abrasions on the deceased's body and a blue-purple abdomen, suggesting poisoning. Coroner Shen could not conduct a thorough examination because he did not bring the necessary equipment. The prosecutor ordered the district head to guard the body pending a second autopsy. Around 2 PM in the afternoon, the prosecutor and others returned for a second autopsy, which confirmed that the death was due to poisoning.

Bomb Explosion Injures Several People 101

Yesterday (the 8th) at 2 PM, a bomb suddenly exploded at the back entrance of the residence of Hu Yuanren at No. 1 Jiangyuan Lane, Chang'an Bridge, outside the North Gate of this city. The sound was deafening. Shen Hongxing, an apprentice at Wu Gonghe Firecracker Shop, was killed on the spot. Shen was 12 years old and from Yanqiao, in the fifth district. Zhu Zhang, a resident at No. 3 (over 70 years old), had her right leg injured. Zhu Yindu's beloved seven-year-old son, Sun Bao, was injured in the head and face. Chen Adu's six-year-old son, Agou, was injured in the eyes and body. A waiter from Fengyuan Noodle Shop (21 years old) was injured in the shoulder. All four were sent to the Brothers Hospital and Puren Hospital for treatment. Their injuries were severe, and their lives were in danger. The explosion caused the brick ground to sink more than a foot deep, and nearby walls and telephone lines were damaged, riddled with holes like a honeycomb. Two toilet and tile rooms also collapsed. Cheng Yunzhao, a patrol officer from the Fifth Public Security Bureau, immediately went to investigate after hearing the news. Chen, the director of the Public Security Bureau, also sent police officers to investigate. Residents there said there were two accounts: One was that Shen Hongxing, an apprentice at Wu Gonghe Firecracker Shop, was playing with gunpowder, causing the explosion. Another was that someone threw a bomb. The Fifth Public Security Bureau took Wu Xiyuan, the owner of Wu Gonghe Shop, to the bureau for further investigation. Wu Rongmo, the head of the fourth district in the north, reported and requested an autopsy.

Changshu Young Woman Commits Suicide by Drowning in Well 102

Ren Cai, a young woman originally from Jiangbei, was 26 years old. She married a doctor from her hometown, but he died not long after. Cai became destitute and wandered around. Two years ago, she came to Changshu, where her life became even more difficult. She became acquainted with and cohabited with Ren Jinsong, a rickshaw puller. The woman had two children, one nine years old and the other six. It was difficult for Ren to support the whole family of four with his rickshaw pulling. So, the woman set up a small stall near Fangqiao, which allowed them to barely make a living. Unfortunately, her lover, Jinsong, succumbed to temptation and turned to theft. Recently, he stole something from a Mr. Li from the North Gate and was arrested by the police and imprisoned. The woman, filled with shame and anxiety, committed suicide by drowning herself in a well. At first, those nearby did not notice Cai's disappearance. It was not until the afternoon of the seventh that a hotel apprentice found her body in the well while drawing water. The authorities were notified, and an autopsy and funeral arrangements were made. Her lover, who is in custody, is being kept in the dark, as the authorities fear he will be distraught.

Changzhou Exhibition of Famous Calligraphers and Painters a Great Success 103

Qian Zhenhuang, a great calligrapher and former Qing dynasty Jinshi, has calligraphy that is bold and unconventional. Zhao Anzhi, a renowned painter from Piling, is a promising young scholar with a great reputation. He has participated in art competitions in Europe and the United States, winning various awards. Zhao is dedicated to the Song and Yuan dynasties, not adhering to any one school, but integrating the strengths of all schools, creating a unique style. The joint exhibition of these two artists at the First Park can be described as a perfect match and is highly praised by the local gentry.

Nantong Salt Smugglers Fighting in Dongyu Town 104

A large group of salt smugglers clashed on the beach in Dongyu Town for unknown reasons. Three people were killed. After the court's prosecutor arrived for an autopsy, the bodies were claimed. In Qinzao, three miles northeast of the city, 3,000 villagers gathered on the seventh to protest conscription, destroying the township office. The Public Security Bureau has dispatched a team to suppress the protest.

Hangzhou Planning to Establish Agricultural Warehouses in Various Counties 105

In order to regulate rural production activities and provide financial support to farmers, the Zhejiang Construction Department plans to borrow one million yuan from the Agricultural Bank of China to help various counties establish agricultural warehouses. It invited agricultural experts Qu Jingzhou, Xu Yuanruo, and others from Shanghai to Hangzhou for discussions. The director of the Cooperative Office, Tang Xunze, accompanied them to various counties, including Tonglu, Jinhua, Lanxi, Zhuji, and Haining, for inspection. They returned to the province yesterday. As the counties do not have farmers' banks or cooperative societies, and handle small-scale agricultural product mortgage loans, which have a considerable foundation, they will draft measures and submit them to the provincial government for approval and implementation.

Zhejiang to Borrow Funds to Purchase 50,000 Dan of Surplus Cocoons 106

This spring, the Zhejiang province has promoted improved silkworm eggs in 32 counties and cities, issuing 1.3 million sheets of eggs, which have been claimed by the counties for rearing. According to reports, the silkworm season is going well. The earliest cocoons from Shengxian and Xinchang will be available by the end of the month. The Silk Association has lent out over 1,200 new silk reeling machines, which have been transported to various silk factories for installation and will be completed by the end of the month. New silk reeling will begin in early next month. The Zhejiang province will have a surplus of 50,000 to 60,000 dan of cocoons after the spring harvest. The government has decided to borrow funds from banks to purchase them itself.

Ningbo Fishermen in Shenjiamen Stage Large-Scale Petition 107

On the afternoon of the third, the Yantian (salt) Affairs Tax Police Team in Shenjiamen, Dinghai, seized six Shaoxing salted seafood boats while inspecting salted seafood boats in Donghengtang. The fish salt on the upper layer was mixed with discolored chaff, and the lower layer was all white salt, which suggested they were evading the taxes. The six boat masters, Wang Guozhong, Hong Xinmin, Jiang Qinglin, Lü Waqing, Wang Jincan, and Lü Acai, were detained. Shaoxing fishermen were outraged that their fish salt, which had already changed color after weighing, was seized and the people were detained. Three hundred Shaoxing fishermen gathered, each holding a lit incense stick, and requested assistance from the local Chamber of Commerce. The Chamber of Commerce sent representatives to negotiate with the Tax Police Team. Captain Huang Yuanxun, fearing that the matter would escalate, went to the Dinghai district headquarters for instructions. The six detained boatmen are temporarily being held at the local Public Security Branch. The fishermen, feeling unexpectedly oppressed, have decided to join forces with various fish stalls and associations to appeal to judicial and higher-level salt affairs authorities. It remains to be seen how this will be resolved.

Jiaxing Brothers Fighting Kill Mother 108

Lu Mao Guniang, a farmer from the Jiangjiage area of Luopu Township in Xizha Li, Xinji Town, Jiaxing, had a verbal argument with her brother on the afternoon of the seventh, which led to a physical altercation. Lu Mao Guniang held an iron hoe, and her brother held a fish fork. Their mother stepped in to try to stop them, and Lu Mao Guniang accidentally struck her mother in the temple with the iron hoe. The mother fell to the ground and died instantly. The scene was gruesome. The two brothers, realizing they had caused a disaster, fled immediately. Bao Wei Lu Er reported the incident to the Xinji Public Security Bureau. The police took Lu Mao Guniang's lover and her young son to the bureau. Lu Mao Guniang's brother was also arrested. On the eighth, local medical examiners were sent to examine the body. Lu Mao Guniang, who is still at large, is being searched for in different locations.

Local News

China General Chamber of Industry Electrically Requests Curb on North China Smuggling 109

Various Organizations Including the Association of Machine Industries (機聯會) Hold Meetings to Discuss the Matter

The China General Chamber of Industry convened its Executive Committee at 115 Hankou Road at 4 PM yesterday to discuss the issues of North China smuggling and opposing the reduction of import tariffs. Members present were Dai Gengxin, Hu Xiyuan, Yao Xizhou, Wang Yunwu, Weng Yousan, Zhu Gengtao, Cai Shengbai, Wu Yunxu, Wang Qiyu, Wang Yaochen, Lu Fei Bohong, Guo Shun, Xu Guanqun, and Xu Xiaochu. Secretary General Wang Zhisheng, Chairman Guo Shun, and recorder Wu Shuliang of the Chamber were present as observers. The results of the discussions were as follows:

Regarding the increasingly rampant smuggling in North China, which will seize the entire national market if it continues, it was decided to electrically request the government to quickly adopt effective measures to strictly crack down on it.

Regarding the report that the government is considering reducing the import tariffs on sugar and rayon, it was decided to handle it together with the smuggling issue.

Uphold Tariff Rates

The China General Chamber of Industry electrically addressed the central government, stating: "To Premier Jiang, Vice Premier Kong, Minister of Finance Kong, and Minister of Industry Wu of the Nanjing Executive Yuan: The smuggling in North China has caused alarm among industrialists and merchants across the country. It poses a grave threat to our national production enterprises. At a time when all industries are declining, it is already difficult to maintain them, let alone withstand such a major blow. Recently, it has become increasingly rampant, spreading almost throughout the country. If this continues, not only will our national goods market be completely seized, but it will also affect our country's tariff revenue, causing untold harm. As the central hub for domestic industries and merchants, the association is responsible for leading and safeguarding the national industry. Alarmed by the situation, we cannot remain silent. Therefore, we dare to electrically request your esteemed departments to quickly adopt effective measures to strictly crack down on smuggling and maintain the original tariff rates in order to protect the national economy. This would be a great fortune for the people and industry. Respectfully submitted by the entire Executive Committee of the China General Chamber of Industry, Guo Shun, Cai Shengbai, Hu Xiyuan, Wang Qiyu, Zhu Gengtao, Wu Yunxu, Dai Gengxin, Lao Jingxiu, Wang Yunwu, Lu Fei Bohong, Zai Boqi, Xu Guanqun, Xu Xiaochu, Yao Xijiu, Weng Yousan, Yan Qingxiang, Wang Yaochen, Li Yunxian, Gan Zhangpeng, Qian Chengxu, Zhan Jingtang, et al."

Industry and Commerce Organizations Meet Separately

The Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factory Joint Association believes that the issue of smuggling and the central government's proposed reduction of import tariffs may drive industry and commerce to the brink of bankruptcy. Therefore, it held an extraordinary Executive Committee meeting at 8 PM last night to discuss countermeasures. In addition, the National Goods Factory Joint Association, the China National Products Manufacturers Joint Association, the China National Goods Maintenance Association, the Citizens' Promotion of National Goods Association, the China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperative Association, the Shanghai National Goods Movement Joint Association, the Citizens' National Goods Year Movement Committee, and other industry and commerce organizations, as well as various industry guilds, are scheduling meetings to discuss countermeasures due to the impact on the national goods industry.

Total of Over 700 Cases Worth More Than 140,000 Yuan

Since smuggling from North China has affected South China, Shanghai has become the final destination for smuggled goods. Disputes often arise during each seizure. Fortunately, the customs and railway personnel handled the matter peacefully together.

Three Announcements from the Jianghai Customs 112

Issuance of Transit Certificates for Confiscated Goods by Customs

Measures for Taxing Imported Broken Rice and Mixed Products

Order from the Ministry of Finance to Exempt Import Taxes on Automobiles

Tang Haian, the Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, and Baron Sen, the Tax Commissioner, have issued two announcements regarding the issuance of transit certificates for confiscated goods by customs, separate regulations for imported broken rice and its mixed products, and exemption of transit taxes on automobiles.

The first announcement states: "In order to facilitate the transit of goods purchased by merchants from the customs to various locations, this customs office has specially prepared transit certificates for use. The purchasing merchant should prepare an application stating the destination and date and submit it to this customs office for issuance. Upon arrival of the goods at the designated location, the original certificate should be returned to this customs office for cancellation. All merchants are hereby notified. This announcement is hereby made."

Announcement Two: "The measures for taxing imported 'broken rice' have been repeatedly announced by this customs office. Now, in accordance with the order from the Ministry of Finance, starting from April 10th of this year, all imported broken rice will be taxed at the same rate as rice. Mixed products of sugar and broken rice will be taxed separately according to the respective mixing components. Mixed products of rice and broken rice will be taxed at the same rate as rice. The determination of the mixing components of broken rice and sugar will be based on weight. All merchants are hereby notified. This announcement is hereby made."

Announcement Three: "In accordance with the order from the Ministry of Finance, starting from May 1st of this year, all transit taxes on automobiles will be exempted. All merchants are hereby notified. This announcement is hereby made." Superintendent Tang Haian, Tax Commissioner Baron Sen

He Shangping of the Silkworm Improvement Association Returns to Shanghai After Inspecting Zhejiang's Silkworm Season 113

Talks About Silkworm Seasons in Various Places Being in the Second Stage

Farmers' Interest in Silkworm Breeding Gradually Increases This Year

He Shangping, a member of the Silkworm Improvement Association of the National Economic Commission, has returned to Shanghai after inspecting the spring silkworm situation in the Zhejiang area last month. According to Mr. He's statement to a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency, this year, Zhejiang province has released a total of 1.25 million sheets of improved silkworm eggs, an increase of 500,000 sheets compared to last year. The amount of cocoon production will also increase by more than 100,000 dan. Therefore, it is sufficient to prove that farmers' interest in the silkworm breeding industry has gradually increased. The silkworm season in Zhejiang is now in the second stage. Shengxian, Xiaoshao, and other places in eastern Zhejiang are a few days earlier than Hangzhou and other places in western Zhejiang. The recent bad weather is not having a significant impact as it is still in the early larval stage.

The Post Office Has Set Up A Mail Collection and Distribution Office Inside The Venue

The Water Company Will Display Models of Machinery and Parts

Since the Shanghai International Exhibition, which is being held in Shanghai, has been actively prepared, it has been supported by various parties and is progressing smoothly. Clearly Define the Power of Trade Associations, Drawing Lessons from Neighboring Countries

Huang Chaolong to Establish National Products Introduction Center in Surabaya 117

Plans to Establish a Sample Exhibition Center

Mr. Huang Chaolong, chairman of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Surabaya, Netherlands East Indies, who recently returned from Nanyang, is very enthusiastic about promoting Chinese goods in Nanyang. Therefore, after returning to China, in addition to visiting factories in various places, he also contacted national products organizations. Mr. Huang plans to set up a National Products Exhibition Hall in Surabaya, and his plan is quite large. After consulting with organizations such as the China National Products Production and Sales Cooperation Association, they all advocated establishing a sample exhibition center, with a scale that does not need to be too large, but must be established in major commercial ports to widely promote it. Therefore, this matter is still under negotiation. Mr. Huang also intends to organize a National Products Introduction Center in Surabaya, which has been agreed to by the China National Products Introduction General Office. However, the Surabaya authorities have very strict restrictions on the import of foreign goods, adhering to old rules. The import trade is still controlled by their nationals, and our compatriots are only second merchants. Now Mr. Huang is determined to break this old rule to improve trade relations with our country. He has obtained the consent of the authorities, but the imported goods must be exchanged for local products, which is a kind of trade protection policy for the area. However, according to surveys, Surabaya's trade with our country has always been a surplus, and its main product is sugar. Therefore, if the principle of bartering is implemented, the amount of national products transported to Surabaya can be increased. It is reported that the capital of the introduction center is set at 200,000 yuan, and the General Office has agreed to ship the goods there once the capital is raised and the organization is established.

New Auxiliary Coins Widely Promoted 119

Over 3,330,000 Yuan Already Cast and Issued

According to the Central News Agency, the Ministry of Finance ordered the Central Mint to cast and issue new auxiliary coins, which are being exchanged and issued by the Central Bank. Currently, they are being widely promoted in major cities and towns in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, as well as in important cities and towns across the country with branches of the Central Bank. According to the factory's issuance figures as of May 1st, the auxiliary coins that have been released from the factory include 11.16 million half-cent copper coins, 27.34 million one-cent copper coins, 6.8 million five-cent nickel coins, 1.9 million ten-cent nickel coins, and 860,000 twenty-cent nickel coins. Together with the various auxiliary coins cast during the trial casting, a total of 83.74 million coins have been produced, totaling 131.8 million coins, with a total value of 3,334,800 yuan. Currently, because the mint no longer casts silver coins, except for casting a small number of factory bars, all work is focused on casting various auxiliary coins in order to promote them nationwide. The old copper coins and silver dimes collected by the mint are stored within the facility and not melted down for recasting, as the existing copper materials are sufficient for current use.

Total Value of Foreign Trade in the First Quarter Increased Compared to Last Year 128

But the Import Surplus Still Exceeds 38.14 Million Yuan

According to Shen Shi News Agency, the main export goods in the country's foreign trade this year are tung oil, raw and processed hides, and leather goods. The secondary goods include sesame, wool, peanuts, goose eggs, tea, silk, satin, cloth, tin, antimony, tungsten, ore, etc. The main imported goods are metals, ore, machinery, tools, paints, and dyes. According to the General Affairs Department of the Jianghai Customs Office, the total export value for the first quarter of this year (January to March) was 165,214,478 yuan, an increase of over 29 million yuan compared to the 135 million yuan in the same period last year. The total import value was 203,356,197 yuan, a sharp decrease of over 50 million yuan compared to the 254 million yuan in the same period last year. The import surplus was 38,141,719 yuan. Comparing the import value of 97,294,558 yuan and the export value of 39,046,553 yuan for March of last year with the import value of 79,176,369 yuan and the export value of 48,186,299 yuan for March of this year, and the import value of 63,229,532 yuan and the export value of 46,358,921 yuan for February of this year, the import value for March decreased compared to the same period last year but increased compared to February. The export value increased compared to both the same period last year and February.
