Shanghai Citizen Training Office Established; Issues Open Letter to Shanghai Citizens 129

In order to promote local autonomy and political tutelage, the municipal government has established the Shanghai Citizen Training Office, appointing Wu Xingya, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, as the director, Li Xiangqi and Jiang Huaisu as the deputy directors, and Wang Shaoqi, Secretary of the Municipal Government, as the general secretary. Li Xiangqi, the deputy director, concurrently serves as the general captain, and Tao Yishan has been appointed as the deputy general captain. The internal staff are all transferred from the various organs affiliated with the municipal government. The office location has been designated as No. 158 Jinji Road, and operations began on the 20th of last month. All plans have been prepared and are expected to be implemented within this month. The government issued an open letter to the citizens of Shanghai yesterday, stating: Dear citizens, the draft constitution, which is the fundamental plan of the Republic of China, has been promulgated, and the National Assembly will be convened on a set date. In the near future, the constitutional era that we have been looking forward to will be fully realized. However, the nation in the constitutional era requires citizens with sufficient common sense, strong bodies, and a disciplined and organized society. In other words, it requires local autonomy to be well-managed to serve as the foundation for national construction. Sun Yat-sen's National Construction Plan stipulates that during the tutelage period, the government should guide the people's ability to govern themselves. The Shanghai Municipal Government is the organ responsible for local tutelage in Shanghai. Now, in order to rapidly complete the tutelage work and promote local autonomy, the Shanghai Citizen Training Office has been specially established to train the citizens of Shanghai to become healthy citizens, which shows how much the government values ​​this matter. The training methods have been generally determined. All healthy citizens between the ages of eighteen and thirty-five living in the city area will be called for training in stages, each stage lasting two or three months. Upon completion of the training, the government will issue certificates. The scale of each training session will be between three thousand and five thousand people. The training time is stipulated before 9:00 AM and after 5:00 PM, so as not to interfere with the current work time of the citizens. All plans have now been fully prepared, and the first phase will begin within five months. Citizens who are called up are expected to report to the designated police station on time and according to their assigned teams, because enthusiastic participation in training will be rewarded, and those who evade training will be punished. In addition to the general methods, we also have a method to facilitate group training. If the various trade associations, hometown associations, companies, schools, factories, labor unions, and other professional groups in the city have a large number of people, if they can all voluntarily organize separately and request training, we can organize and train them based on their existing organization. We expect to complete the first phase of training in July of this year, and then begin the second phase. At the same time, Shanghai will pilot autonomy and implement the Baojia system. In the future, all Bao and Jia chiefs will naturally be elected from organized and trained citizens to form the foundation of Shanghai's autonomy. If we want the country to be strong, we must revitalize our national spirit, especially in Shanghai, where the social atmosphere is so decadent, which requires a kind of stimulation. Therefore, we hope that the leaders of various industries should lead their people to receive training, and parents and elder brothers should urge their children to receive training. Shop owners or managers should assign their employees and partners to receive training, and others should also voluntarily request to join the training. In short, "the rise and fall of the nation are the responsibility of every citizen." National affairs are our duty, and everyone should enthusiastically promote everything that is beneficial to the country and society, and be willing to sacrifice personal interests. Dear citizens, we should feel that our responsibility is great and our personal future is promising at a time when the country is in serious difficulty. Do not hesitate or wait any longer. You should register as soon as possible and wait to be assigned to receive this glorious training.

Shanghai Goods Exported to US in First Four Months of This Year 130

Total Value Exceeds US$8,460,000

The US Consulate General in Shanghai released statistics on Thursday, stating that the total value of Shanghai's exports to the United States, the Philippines, and Hawaii in the first four months of this year was US$8,462,829, of which the Philippines accounted for US$433,984 and Hawaii accounted for US$15,065. In these four months, the United States purchased US$33,442 worth of Chinese tea and US$17,021 worth of vegetable powder. The largest business was still oilseeds and vegetable oils, of which sesame accounted for US$1,095,920, tung oil accounted for US$955,017, and cottonseed oil accounted for US$189,899. Textiles accounted for US$1,628,636, of which waste cotton accounted for US$211,512, embroidered cloth accounted for US$466,511, carpets accounted for US$98,399, human hair accounted for US$109,064, and straw hats accounted for US$182,028. Raw silk accounted for US$94,394, tin ingots accounted for US$396,580, and firecrackers accounted for only US$143. The main goods exported to the Philippines were food, including fresh eggs worth US$39,940, ham worth US$30,614, soybeans worth US$41,370, and cotton products worth US$200,000. The main goods exported to Hawaii were embroidery and porcelain.

Xingye Trust Company: Launches Real Estate Trust Business 134

Establishes Seven Regulations...Officially Announces Commencement of Operations Yesterday

According to sources, the Shanghai Xingye Trust Company, in order to revive the market and stimulate finance, has begun to handle real estate trust business. There are a total of seven regulations for its business methods, which are recorded as follows:

Motive for Operation: The company, considering that since the Ministry of Finance implemented the monetary policy, the financial situation of various industries across the country has shifted from a gloomy environment to a bright outlook, and that it will not be difficult to move towards prosperity in the future. However, to revive various industries, real estate business must be stimulated first. Although the Municipal Finance Bureau previously sent letters to both the banking and money industries, encouraging them to undertake real estate mortgage loans, and instructed them to list Chinese-owned real estate as reserve assets, it is still difficult for various firms and banks to handle this business universally. In order to stimulate market capital, the company has specially launched real estate trust business, and can accept and handle real estate in both the Chinese and foreign concessions. The company issued an announcement yesterday stating, "To facilitate property owners, we have agreed with the Finance and Land Bureaus to handle the above-mentioned business. (Details of the trust methods are below.) Procedures are simple, time is quick, and fees are extremely low. If entrusted, we would be most welcoming. Printed regulations are available upon request."

Trust Methods: The regulations for the company's property department in handling real estate trust business are recorded as follows: Replacing and Obtaining Land Deeds: When replacing and obtaining land deeds, the required property certificates must be deposited with the company, and the company will issue a receipt. Unless there are disputes over property rights, the company will, based on the complexity of the matter and the time required, handle the application on behalf of the client and collect all fees stipulated by the various bureaus, which will be borne by the client. Surveying, Dividing, or Merging Land Deeds: The required property certificates must be deposited with the company, and the company will complete the application and obtain the deeds in due course. Transferring Ownership or Mortgage Registration: The property certificates must be deposited with the company, and a transfer application or mortgage registration application must be signed to handle the transfer or registration on behalf of the client. The property certificates will be returned after completion the next day. All fees stipulated by the various bureaus will be borne by the client. Paying Land Value Tax and Field Tax on Behalf of Client: The required documents and taxes must be handed over to the company for payment on behalf of the client. The date on which the company receives the payment will be considered the date of tax payment. Selling Real Estate on Behalf of Client: The property certificates or their drawings must be sent to the company for registration (the original will be returned), and a letter of authorization must be signed, stating the minimum price per mu, so that the company can find buyers on behalf of the client. As for large properties that need to be divided for sale, the client must hand over all property certificates to the company for division on behalf of the client, with expenses borne by the client. The company may sell part or all of it. If property disputes arise in the real estate entrusted for sale, the seller shall be responsible. As for the fees payable to the various bureaus, they shall be borne by the buyer or seller respectively, in accordance with the regulations of the various bureaus. Purchasing Real Estate on Behalf of Client: Specify the area and price limit and register with the company, or submit one-tenth of the price limit as a deposit and sign a letter of authorization. If the transaction cannot be completed within the specified period, the deposit will be returned, along with interest at an annual rate of 5%. As for the fees payable to the various bureaus upon completion of the transaction, they shall also be borne by the buyer or seller respectively, in accordance with the regulations. Consultation: For all real estate matters in Shanghai, inquiries can be made by letter or in person. The company will provide detailed replies. (Note) These regulations may be revised from time to time without further notice, but shall not affect cases that have already been entrusted.

Completely Levying Tax on Foreign Broken Rice 136

Gu Xin'yi Returns to Shanghai from Beijing

Has Explained to the Rice Industry

Regarding the issue of levying taxes on foreign broken rice, the Municipal Bean and Rice Industry Association previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance, proposing to follow the precedent of Ningbo, to levy a full tax by the Ministry of Finance. It was previously stipulated that items not listed would still be subject to half tax. The request was rejected by the Ministry of Finance. Gu Xin'yi, chairman of the Bean and Rice Industry Association, recently went to Beijing again to make a request. Gu has now returned to Shanghai. It is understood that the Shanghai side had previously ordered 100,000 bags of broken rice from foreign merchants, of which 60,000 bags have arrived in Shanghai and 40,000 bags will arrive soon. The Ministry of Finance's reason for not following the Ningbo precedent was that the foreign broken rice ordered by Ningbo was for disaster relief purposes and not comparable to general business circumstances. After Gu's explanation to the rice industry, all the foreign broken rice that has arrived has been subject to full taxes in accordance with the Ministry of Finance's new regulations, and goods have been picked up from customs. The remaining 40,000 bags are also prepared to pay full taxes. It is also understood that importing foreign rice is no longer cost-effective at current market prices, so the import of foreign rice will be reduced in the future.

Ministry of Industry Bans Businesses Similar to the Fish Market

However, 13 fresh and frozen fish businesses, including Qianfeng Firm, have not yet joined. The Ministry of Industry and the Fish Market have sent telegrams and letters respectively, earnestly requesting the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to advise them. A reporter from the Xin Xin News Agency has recorded the situation as follows:

Investigation into Fish Firms Joining the Market: The fish firms in Shanghai that have joined the Fish Market as wholesalers and brokers include 17 members of the Shanghai Fresh Fish Industry and Fresh and Frozen Fish Industry Guild, including Shen Baoji, Hengtai, Qu Changshun, Tongrenchang, Yurun, Yongtai, Huifeng, Fenghao, Fuji, Shunda, Yuanli, Hongfa, Yuanchang, Binghui, Dahe, Yuanmao, and Jiuji. The 13 members of the Shanghai Fresh and Frozen Fish Industry Guild that have not joined, including Shengji Firm, Qianfeng Firm, Gongda Firm, Taichang Firm, Dechang Firm, Hongyuan Firm, Gongshun Firm, Xiangshun Firm, Yuantong Firm, Dacheng Firm, Qiafeng Firm, Hongchang Firm, and Yuanyu Firm, are still operating as usual at their original location at No. 16, Xiaodongmen.

Ministry of Industry Cables Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Advise: The Ministry of Industry cables the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating, "Please note that Article 3 of the Shanghai Fish Market Regulations approved by the Executive Yuan stipulates that after the market opens, no other businesses of the same or similar nature may operate in the Shanghai area. Furthermore, Article 2 of the operating regulations stipulates that the first transaction of all marine, freshwater, saltwater, and dried fish products imported into Shanghai must be conducted at the Fish Market. The market is scheduled to open on the 11th of this month. Please earnestly inform the fresh and frozen river fish industries to deeply understand the Central Government's intention to improve fish market transactions and to faithfully implement them. The Ministry of Industry." The Fish Market sends a letter stating, "Regarding the Shanghai Fish Market, it was established in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Industry. It has now been scheduled to open on the 11th of this month. In accordance with the regulations, after the market opens, no other businesses of the same or similar nature may operate in the Shanghai area. Moreover, this market is mainly operated by the Ministry of Industry and is not purely a commercial organization. In addition to the fact that this association has repeatedly advised members of the fresh and frozen industry guild to join, we are writing to request your association to promptly invite personnel from the Shanghai Fresh Fish Industry Guild to earnestly advise and guide them to continue joining the market in order to avoid misunderstandings and protect their business. We would be grateful for your attention to this matter."

Inviting the Industry to Talk Today: After receiving telegrams from the Ministry of Industry and letters from the Board of Directors of the Shanghai Fish Market, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce specially submitted the matter to the 89th Standing Committee meeting of the association the day before yesterday for discussion. It was resolved that the chairman of the association, Yu Zuoting, would be publicly recommended to invite representatives of the Fresh and Frozen Fish Industry Guild to talk. Yu decided to invite representatives of various fish firms in the fresh and frozen fish industry to talk at the Chamber of Commerce at Tianhougong Bridge at 2:00 PM this afternoon, earnestly advising them to understand the Central Government's intention to improve the fish industry, cooperate together, and jointly seek the development of their business.

Ministry of Industry Bans Similar Businesses: The Ministry of Industry issued Announcement No. 416 regarding the prohibition of businesses similar to the fish market, stating, "The Shanghai Fish Market established by this Ministry is a joint government-business operation approved by the Central Political Conference and resolved by the Executive Yuan, and the joint government-business Shanghai Fish Market Co., Ltd. is operated in accordance with the articles of association filed with the National Government for record. Article 3 of the articles of association states: 'After the market opens, no other businesses of the same or similar nature may operate in the Shanghai area.' Furthermore, Article 2 of the market's operating regulations specifies the types of fish and seafood traded at the fish market, as follows: 1. Marine fish; 2. Freshwater fish; 3. Salted and dried fish; 4. Other aquatic products. The first transaction of the aforementioned fish and seafood imported into Shanghai must be conducted at the Fish Market. The market is scheduled to open on May 11th. This announcement is hereby issued for your compliance. Minister Wu Dingchang."

Aquatic Students Visit the Market: A delegation of ten students from the manufacturing group of the Hebei Provincial Aquatic Products Vocational School, led by their professor Sun Muyuan, arrived in Shanghai on the 7th aboard the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Tai Shun ship. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, led by Sun, they braved the rain to visit the Shanghai Fish Market of the Ministry of Industry in Jiangxinsha. The general manager of the market, Wang Xiaolai, sent staff to accompany them and visit various departments. The visit concluded at around 11:00 AM. The delegation also visited the Wusong Aquatic Products School yesterday afternoon and plans to stay in Shanghai for a week to visit various factories and new construction projects before returning to Tianjin by sea.

Director of Guangdong Agriculture and Forestry Bureau, Feng Rui, Expresses Opinions on Reducing Sugar Tax 138

Guangdong's Sugar Industry Still Requires Considerable Time to Succeed

Reducing Tariffs Suddenly is Like Weaning an Infant

Feng Rui, Director of the Guangdong Provincial Agriculture and Forestry Bureau and Manager of the Sugarcane Manufacturing Plant, flew to Beijing the day before yesterday to meet with various authorities, report on the latest developments in the Guangdong sugar industry, and inquire about the truth regarding recent reports of foreigners requesting a reduction in sugar taxes. Before his departure, he expressed his opinions on reducing sugar taxes to a reporter from the New Sound News Agency as follows:

Five-Year Plan: We believe that Guangdong's sugar industry can compete with the well-established sugar industries of Java, Cuba, the Philippines, and Taiwan, and if given a little more time and opportunity, it will certainly be possible. Guangdong's land and climate have been repeatedly investigated and studied by sugar experts William G. Hallo, Prof. KingDr., and Bannier, who all believe that they are suitable for developing the sugar industry. The points that should be emphasized are the improvement of sugarcane varieties and the improvement of methods such as planting, fertilization, and irrigation. This section is also being planned and carried out, and will be completed within five years. The British government levies a standard tax of 11 shillings and 8 pence on every 112 pounds of sugar, in addition to the following surtaxes. During the period from 1924 to 1927, the tax was 19 shillings and 6 pence per 112 pounds; from 1928 to 1930, 13 shillings; from 1931 to 1933, 6 shillings and 6 pence; and from 1933 to the present, 6 shillings and 6 pence. In order to protect its sugar industry, the British Indian government decided to levy a tax of 9 rupees and 1 anna per 112 pounds, starting in 1931, for a period of ten years. Since its implementation, production has increased from 60,000 tons in 1931 to 600,000 tons. The development of the sugar industry depends on technology and science. If the foundation of technology and science is not solid, the cost cannot be reduced, and it will be difficult to match other countries. According to the experiences of Java, the Philippines, Taiwan, and other places, the solution to technical and other problems takes at least five years. From this, it can be seen that the protection period for our country's sugar industry cannot be less than five years. At present, Guangdong's sugar industry is in the process of improvement, and the cost of white sugar is as high as 20 yuan per picul, so even with tariff protection, the profit is very small.

Tariff Protection: What foundation is Guangdong's sugar industry built upon? The establishment and existence of Guangdong's sugar industry is based on protective tariffs. All plans are based on tariff rates. Without this, the current Guangdong sugar industry would be unable to survive. Therefore, the Guangdong sugar industry is like a newborn infant being fed by tariffs. Reducing tariffs suddenly is like cutting off its food and driving it to compete with the strong and robust sugar industries of Java and Taiwan. The result is foreseeable. Attitude of Foreign Sugar Industry: Over the past two years, important personnel and experts from the foreign sugar industry have come to Guangdong one after another, paying close attention to the sugar industry. After their investigation, they all believe that all difficulties can be overcome within a few years and success can be achieved. Its production factors, such as fertile land and suitable climate, are all available compared to Java, Taiwan, and other places. With tariff protection and five years of effort, Guangdong sugar can not only supply the entire country's consumption, but also be exported to foreign countries and compete in the world market. Furthermore, reducing tax rates will not only affect Guangdong's sugar industry, but also the industrialists in other sugarcane-producing provinces, such as Fujian, Zhejiang, and Sichuan, will also terminate their investment plans.

Sugar Industry Facilities: Guangdong's three-year construction plan and sugar industry facilities. Guangdong's economic situation is that every year, more than 100 million yuan worth of cotton and cotton fabrics, 200 million yuan worth of grains and rice, 50 million yuan worth of oils, and 30 million yuan worth of various fertilizers are imported from home and abroad. In addition to sugar, there are very few other major export goods. Therefore, Guangdong's three-year construction plan is almost entirely focused on the development of the sugar industry. 50 million yuan has been invested, of which 40 million yuan has not yet been paid to the contractors of various sugar factories, such as the Skoda Ironworks in the Czech Republic and the Honolulu Iron Works. The payment method is set for three or five years, paid in monthly installments. These foreign manufacturers are deeply convinced that Guangdong's sugar industry will be successful if given a five-year tariff protection period. The Guangdong authorities are doing their best to raise funds and divert all surplus tax revenue and military reserve funds to sugar industry construction. If it fails without protection, the entire province's economy will be affected, the sugar industry will go bankrupt, and the lives of millions of people connected to it will be seriously disrupted. It is permissible to say that if the sugar tax is slightly reduced, other industries will inevitably demand the same, and the capital sector will terminate domestic industrial investment. I fear that the example of sugar tax reduction will be applied to all commodities.

Comparison of Tax Rates: Comparison of import tax rates for sugar in various countries. Germany levies a tax of 71.32 per metric quintal, the Czech Republic 71.15, Austria 59.58, Hungary 95.29, France 56.18, Belgium 90.48, the Netherlands 92.29, Poland 151.46, Italy 151.48, Romania 34.59, Estonia 7.59, British India 22.30, and China 21.76. Comparing the import tax rates for sugar in the thirteen countries listed in the table, the highest are Italy and Poland, at 151.48 yuan per metric quintal, and the lowest is our country, at 21.76 yuan per metric quintal. The tax rates in Italy and Poland are six times higher than ours, and the average tax rate in various countries is 72.81 yuan, which is three times higher than ours. Therefore, in any case, it is difficult to reduce our country's sugar tariffs.

Must Be Protected: The number of people who depend on the old and new sugar industries. The country's annual sugar production is 15 million piculs, including the slab sugar produced by old-style sugar mills in Guangdong, Sichuan, Fujian, and Guangxi. The number of people working directly and indirectly in the sugar industry is at least 10 million. The output in 1930 suddenly dropped to 4 million piculs because of low tax rates and cheap foreign sugar being dumped in large quantities. After the sugar tax rate was changed in 1932, the sugar industry has had the opportunity to revive. If the current tax rate is reduced, the old and new sugar industries will be destroyed without a trace. Our country will once again be forced to purchase the same amount of foreign sugar as in 1930. As a result, our country's silver reserves will be reduced by at least 120 million yuan per year due to the purchase of sugar, and at the same time, the trade situation will become even more unbalanced. Therefore, for the sake of the future revival of the sugar industry and for the sake of the country's economic future, the domestic sugar industry must be vigorously protected.

Apprentice Dies Tragically at Wuhua Shoe Factory; Autopsy Conducted 145

Confirmed as Stabbed to Death by Scissors; Perpetrator's Confession Attempts to Evade Responsibility

At 6:30 AM the day before yesterday, a stabbing occurred at the Wuhua Shoe Factory in Yuanmao Lane, Arabella Street, due to a dispute over work, resulting in the death of an apprentice. Details of this incident have already been reported in the newspaper. It is now known that the Wuhua Shoe Factory has two plants, an old one at No. 145 North Zhejiang Road and a new one at No. 18 Yuanmao Lane, Arabella Street. The average daily workload for apprentices is 30 pairs of shoe uppers per person. Yesterday morning at 6:30 AM, Yuan Wenzai (21 years old, from Haimen), an apprentice from the new plant, went to the old plant to collect shoe uppers. However, Wei Xianrong (18 years old, from Zhenjiang), an apprentice from the old plant, only gave him 20 pairs, leading to a dispute. Wei reported this to Zhang Jinfa, the bookkeeper in the new plant's accounting room. At that time, Yuan Wenzai had also returned. They encountered each other at the entrance, and Yuan blamed Wei for reporting such a minor matter to the accounting room, leading to a second dispute and mutual assault. Wei suddenly produced a pair of sharp scissors from his person and stabbed Yuan Wenzai five times, hitting vital areas. Yuan collapsed in a pool of blood. Colleagues from the factory, including Wang Kanghui, restrained Wei and reported the incident to the Huishi Police Station, which dispatched officer Li Wenbin to take Wei Xianrong, along with the murder weapon, to the Huishi Police Station for detention. Yuan Wenzai was rushed to Renji Hospital but died on the way due to the severity of his injuries. The body was sent to the Forensic Examination Center on Peel Road. Yesterday morning, Wei Xianrong was transferred to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's lawyer, filed a public prosecution for homicide under Article 271 of the Criminal Law and presented the case, stating that, according to the doctor's examination, the deceased Yuan Wenzai had three wounds on his left chest, two on his left back, and one on the back of his hand, totaling five stab wounds. According to the defendant's confession at the police station, he used the scissors to defend himself because the deceased had punched him first, and he presented the scissors as evidence, stating that there was still blood on them. Under questioning, Wei Xianrong confessed that he was an apprentice at the old Wuhua factory. Yesterday morning, the deceased wanted 30 pairs of shoe uppers, but he only gave him 20 pairs, leading to a conflict. He then reported this to the accounting room, but Yuan followed him and punched him at the entrance of the new factory, leading to a scuffle. Later, the bookkeeper Zhang Jinfa dispersed them, but the deceased suddenly collapsed, accusing him of stabbing him with scissors. He was then restrained by colleagues and taken to the police station. After translation, the presiding judge instructed the defendant to remain in custody for further questioning in seven days. Tang, the prosecutor, arrived at the scene and confirmed that the body had died from stab wounds inflicted before death. He then ordered the body to be handed over to Wang Chengfa, the factory owner of the deceased, with a guarantee.

Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters Organizes Political Prisoner Education Committee 147

Nominates Pan Gongzhan and 24 Others as Committee Members; Adopts Outline and Schedules Group Sessions to Begin Education

According to the Dagong News Agency, the Ministry of Judicial Administration previously suggested to the executive branches of Shanxi and Henan provinces that ideological training and special education should be administered to political prisoners in prisons. This suggestion was adopted at a conference of the Ministry of Judicial Administration and was issued to prison authorities in various regions on December 5th of last year. Upon receiving the order, the Jiangsu Second Prison Branch in this city, in accordance with Proposal No. 85, which stated, "In areas where there is a Penitentiary, the training staff of the Penitentiary may concurrently serve as instructors; in areas without a Penitentiary, personnel from the local high-level Party headquarters may concurrently serve as instructors," sent a letter requesting the Municipal Party Headquarters to handle the matter. After receiving the letter, the Municipal Party Headquarters recognized the importance of training political prisoners and, through a standing committee, appointed education committee members. The first meeting was held yesterday morning at 10:00 AM in the meeting room of the Party Headquarters, where several important matters were resolved. These are detailed below.

First Meeting

The Municipal Political Prisoner Education Committee, appointed by the Municipal Party Headquarters, consists of Zhi Gongzhan, Ying Xingbai, Jiang Huaian, Xing Wan, Lu Jingshi, Lin Meiyan, Mei Hao, Zhang Xiaotong, Yuan Yeyu, Jiang Wenbin, Wu Shuhe, Xu Hongzao, Ling Xianwen, Huang Xianggu, Wu Xianren, Shen Chunhui, Zhu Jiarang, Yang Jialin, Zhang Jianming, Zhu Qifa, Zhong Longzhang, Zhao Shusheng, and He Chengfu, 25 people in total. The first committee meeting was held at 10:00 AM yesterday morning in the meeting room of the Municipal Party Headquarters, chaired by Ying Xingbai and recorded by Shen Chunhui. Matters Reported: Chairman Ying reported on the origins of the committee's formation. Committee Member Zhang Jianming reported on (A) the situation of political prisoners in various prisons and (B) the previous efforts of the Municipal Party Headquarters to send personnel to various prisons for education.

Method of Education

Subsequently, the meeting discussed the method of education and what form it should take. It was resolved to adopt an individual conversation approach. Regarding how political prisoners should be grouped, it was resolved to create a form, send it to various prisons for investigation, and group the prisoners based on their educational background and experience, with each group not exceeding ten people. Regarding how the educational outline should be defined, it was resolved that the educational outline would not be specifically defined, but the following principles would be used as the scope of education: (A) "Belief," (B) "Life," (C) "Politics," and (D) "Economics." The aim is to engage in conversations with each political prisoner and guide them towards the Three Principles of the People. Regarding determining the date for the commencement of education, it was resolved to decide after the investigation and grouping. Jiang Huaisu, Lu Jingshi, and Xing Wan were elected as standing committee members. The rest is omitted.

Organizational Outline

Organizational Outline of the Shanghai Political Prisoner Education Committee: The committee is organized by the Municipal Executive Committee in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Judicial Administration. The purpose of the committee is to implement special education for political prisoners in various prisons. The committee will consist of 25 members, appointed from members of the Municipal Party Headquarters and comrades from across the city. The Municipal Executive Committee will also appoint three standing members and one secretary to handle daily work. Committee members will take turns attending various prisons to educate political prisoners. The topics will be determined in advance by the committee, and an outline will be prepared and sent to each committee member for implementation in order. Committee members must not be absent when it is their turn to attend. The committee may employ staff from the Municipal Party Headquarters to serve as secretaries, etc., but without additional pay. Committee members are unpaid, but they will be reimbursed for transportation expenses when attending education sessions. These regulations will be implemented upon approval by the Municipal Executive Committee.

Shanghai Public Utilities Bureau to Launch Shanghai-Caohejing Public Bus Route 148

Purchasing Twelve New Buses from the United States; Officially Launching Service in Early July

The Shanghai Southern Public Bus Management Office of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, in order to develop urban-rural transportation and facilitate travel for farmers, has decided to launch a public bus route from Shanghai to Caohejing, with official service to begin in early July. Twelve new buses have been purchased from the American Damon Company. Details are as follows:

Designated Route

The route for the Shanghai to Caohejing public bus service has been finalized by the Shanghai Southern Public Bus Management Office. The starting station is Peace Road near the Old City Gate, and the ending station is the west side of Caohejing Town. The route passes through Zhaozhou Road, Xieqiao, Xiexu Road, Dazha Bay, Dapu Bridge, Jiji Bridge, turns into Xietu Road, passes through Xujiahui Town, Hongqiao, and reaches Caohejing Town. The roadbed paving project is being carried out by the Public Works Bureau and is expected to be completed and officially open for traffic in early July of this year.

Connecting Routes

The Shanghai-Caohejing route connects with various routes in the southern Shanghai area managed by the Management Office, such as Route 1 to Longhua, Route 3 to the Circular City Route, Route 4 to the Red Character Xiqiao and the Sixteenth Pier, and the Black Character Dapu Bridge, to the Xiaodongmen and Dadongtou Road routes. Passengers will not encounter difficulties when transferring to other routes. The fare for each stop on the route, as well as for the starting and ending stations, is currently being determined.

Purchasing New Buses

Since the Shanghai Southern Public Bus Management Office took over the commercially operated bus company in the southern Shanghai area in the past, operations on all routes have flourished after the Management Office's dedicated reorganization. The Management Office is now launching a new route to Caohejing, so there are not enough vehicles to allocate. Therefore, twelve new buses have been ordered from the American Damon Company and have already been shipped to Shanghai. The Management Office has contracted with businesses for the construction of the bus bodies and other projects, which are expected to be completed by mid-June.

Late Qing Dynasty Conscripts Form the Bingwu Military Service Memorial Association 150

The volunteers of the 32nd year of the Guangxu era of the former Qing Dynasty initiated the 30th Anniversary of Military Service Memorial held at Tiger Hill in Suzhou. The participants from Shanghai included Sun Chouchong, Ma Jisheng, Gao Wosheng, Ji Sinong, Xu Shizhang, Lu Moyuan, Zhang Gang and other seven people, and they returned to Shanghai yesterday. According to reports, after reporting to No. 51 Banlian Lane on the afternoon of the 2nd, a preparatory meeting was held. On the morning of the 3rd, they went to Anletuan outside Fenghua Gate to pay respects to the tomb of Commander Zhang Diqiu. At noon, a meeting was held at Lengxiang Pavilion in Tiger Hill, with more than 30 people including Yin Shisheng, Su Kunshan, and Peng Bingyi attending. It was resolved to establish the Bingwu Military Service Memorial Association, with the office located at No. 30 Jiyi Lane, Tianjin Road, Shanghai. Sun Chouchong, Ma Jisheng, and Ji Sinong were elected as directors of the general affairs, accounting, and documentation departments. Gatherings will be held once a year and commemorative meetings every five years. Those comrades from various places who did not participate this time can join the association if two members prove that they were indeed conscripts of the 32nd year. No membership fee will be charged. Military officers of that time who wish to join will be honorary members. A group photo was taken in front of the Shanguantang, and a public banquet was held at the Chamber of Commerce office, singing the military songs of that time. In the afternoon, they visited the old barracks and toured the Liuyuan Garden. The next day, they visited famous scenic spots such as Tianping and Lingyan, and Sun Fuji hosted a farewell banquet before they dispersed.

Ningbo Native Association Cables Request to Halt Grave Relocations in Ning Districts 151

The relocation of graves in various Ning districts is being handled too hastily, causing public anxiety, especially in various villages of Yinxian County. The Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai has repeatedly received reports from villagers requesting assistance. It has sent letters and telegrams requesting rectification, as previously reported. It has now been learned that although the relocation of graves in the urban and suburban areas of Yinxian County has been halted, there are rumors that it will continue in the rural areas. Fearing that different policies will lead to misunderstandings, they sent a telegram to the Yinxian County Government yesterday, stating: "We have received your telegram regarding the halt to grave relocations in the urban area of Yin County. We are comforted. According to news reports, you have recently submitted a document to the Special Commissioner's Office stating that the rural areas will continue to be implemented in order to avoid too many changes. Local governance is inconsistent with provincial orders and is not a fundamental solution, causing greater public anxiety. Urban and rural areas should be treated equally, and different policies are not appropriate. We request that you order all townships to immediately halt the relocation until officials, civilians, and merchants have agreed on an overall plan, which is then submitted to the province for approval, before proceeding to avoid further disturbances. Sincerely, Yu Hede and others from the Ningdu Native Association in Shanghai."

Young Women's Christian Association Holds Annual Meeting Yesterday 154

Over One Hundred Chinese and Western Members Attend, Reporting on the Association's Achievements

The Shanghai branch of a Christian Young Women's Christian Association held its 28th annual meeting at its new headquarters at No. 999 Jing'an Temple Road yesterday at 5:00 PM. Attendees included Mrs. He Linyi, president of the association, Mrs. Yu Yingjie, vice president, Liu Wang Liming, and over one hundred Chinese and Western members. The president reported on the association's achievements in the past year, stating that the association was established earlier than any other Young Women's Christian Association in the country. It began engaging in social work in 1904 and was officially established in 1908. It has performed well in the past two or three decades. Since moving to its new headquarters on March 7th of this year, it has made even greater efforts. Looking back on its services to society, it can be divided into eight parts: (1) The Girls' Department, also known as the Huaguang Group, currently has about two hundred members. (2) Job Placement: From 1934 to last year, about four hundred people registered, and about one hundred people found employment. (3) Dormitory: Currently, there are about thirty to forty residents. The monthly rent for each person in a shared room is five yuan. (4) Popular Education: Currently, there are six locations in Pudong, Yangshupu, and Zhaofeng Road, as well as volunteer night schools, which specialize in teaching poor and out-of-school women. Tuition and fees are not charged. Currently, there are nearly one thousand female laborers and students. (5) Membership Department: Divided into adult education classes and group activity classes. Adult education classes include Mandarin, English, Chinese and foreign cooking, and dance. Group organizations include family study groups, group travel lectures. (6) Labor Department: Includes labor women's schools and labor women's activities. (7) International Branch: Dedicated to serving foreign women. (8) Tutoring Classes: Offer courses in Chinese, French, German, English, dance, sports, cooking, handicrafts, typing, and music. After the President's report, the future development policies and estimates of members' work achievements were discussed. Finally, students from Xie Jin Primary School performed songs to add to the entertainment. The meeting adjourned with refreshments at 7:00 PM.

Scarce Pork Supply Leads to Price Increase Yesterday 158

The Fresh Meat Industry Association of this city, citing scarce supply and soaring prices, announced a uniform price increase starting yesterday, averaging four to six cents per pound. Their announcement stated: "Recently, representatives from various districts in the British, French, and American concessions, as well as the surrounding countryside, have repeatedly requested meetings, stating that the current supply of fresh pork is scarce, pork prices are rising daily, and the livelihood of those in the industry is becoming increasingly difficult. As a result, various shops have unanimously requested to close the market for several days in order to uniformly increase prices." In response, it has been verified that the requests are based on factual circumstances. However, closing the market is difficult to approve because we are in the midst of implementing the New Life Movement, and there are many memorial days this month, so how can we selfishly proceed in this way? Furthermore, the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has previously issued a notice to all industry associations in the city, prohibiting unwarranted business closures, which is on record. Therefore, this association convened representatives from all districts in the city on the 7th of this month. Representatives from the British, French, and American concessions, inside and outside the city walls, and from the surrounding countryside, including Fan Deyu, Sun Hongxiang, Chen Longhu, Rong Zhaogang, Wu Gengsheng, Yang Weibai, Yu Jinfu, Xu Jinsheng, Ye Shifan, Rong Qianchu, Gu Ziyun, Zai Jingfu, Huang Shuntang, Fang Yongchu, Huang Zhongqi, Yang Zhicheng, Song Yingui, Zhou Chengxiang, Wu Binglin, Ye Hengxian, Ye Hengshao, Shen Weifu, Gu Shaoqin, and others, a total of over seventy people, were present. The executive committee of this association earnestly dissuaded them from closing the market and immediately agreed to set a uniform market price. It is hoped that all members of the industry in the city will prioritize their livelihoods, protect their own capital, and not act carelessly. They should sell according to the prices agreed upon by the representatives in order to maintain a uniform price throughout the city. On the other hand, we hope you will kindly inform your customers and explain the various difficulties of this industry, hoping for their understanding. The agreed-upon prices are listed below. All prices are based on the market scale. Door sales: Trotters are 36 cents per pound, center cut is 38 cents per pound, ribs and leg are all 40 cents per pound, streaky pork is 34 cents per pound, lard is 32 cents per pound, boneless and skinless all lean meat is 52 cents per pound. Wholesale to taverns, noodle shops, restaurants, rice shops, and Cantonese businesses: leg and ribs are 2 catties 12 ounces per dollar, center cut and trotters are 3 catties, streaky pork and lard are 3 catties 4 ounces, all lean meat is 2 catties.

Man Crushed to Death by Freight Train in Shanghai-Hangzhou 165

At 1:35 PM yesterday afternoon, a locomotive numbered A1218 was dispatched from the locomotive depot at the South Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway to Rijiegang to pick up freight cars and transport them to the South Station for connection to the Hangzhou-bound freight train. As the locomotive passed the fifth kilometer (i.e., the Banlu intersection) of the railway track, a man, about thirty years old, wearing a maroon woolen shirt and cloth shorts, barefoot, was walking on the track and failed to avoid the train. He was crushed in the waist by the locomotive and died instantly. The scene was gruesome. The driver immediately reported to the South Station, which dispatched railway police to investigate and take care of the situation, and ordered the local bailiff to report to the court for inspection, and to summon the deceased's relatives to the station to identify and claim the body, and prepare a coffin for burial.

Records of Two Coroner's Inquests 166

Sudden Death: At about 8:00 PM the night before, a rickshaw with license number 9517, driven by Zhu Kunhai, 40 years old, was hired at Xujiahui Road in the Nanshi area by a young man in his twenties, wearing a black gown and blue trousers, to go to the local court. While traveling near the Sanguantang area on Jiaoning Road, the passenger suddenly fell ill and died. The rickshaw driver, Zhu Kunhai, reported to the local police officer, who reported to the Huining Road Police Station, who reported to the Ximen Branch. The bailiff of the area was ordered to report to the court for inspection. At about 11:00 AM yesterday, the court sent prosecutor Xiao Jinying to conduct the inspection. It was determined that the death was due to a sudden illness. In addition to filling out the death certificate and taking photographs, the bailiff was instructed to prepare a coffin for burial at the Tongren Fuyuantang.

Death on the Road: Police officer Yang Peisheng of the Huining Road No. 48 post discovered an unidentified male corpse at about 11:00 AM in front of the Goping Iron Factory on Xietu Road. The corpse was about 40 years old, wearing a black cloth short jacket, without trousers, barefoot, lying on the road. He immediately reported to the Ximen Branch, which ordered the bailiff to report to the court for inspection. At noon, the court sent prosecutor Xiao Jinying to conduct the inspection. It was determined that the death was due to illness. In addition to filling out the death certificate and taking photographs, the bailiff was instructed to prepare a coffin for burial.

Robbery on Robison Road Yesterday Morning 167

At about 5:00 AM yesterday morning, while the servants were washing dirty utensils at the back door of the Guo family residence at No. 28 Zudeli, Robison Road, Caojiadu, three bandits speaking the Anhui dialect suddenly appeared and carried out a robbery. The bandits were all wearing blue cloth shirts and trousers and carrying pistols. After entering the house, they broke straight into the inner room and threatened the owner to hand over his property. However, although the owner was a foreman, he had no savings, so the bandits searched thoroughly and only managed to steal 65 yuan in banknotes and more than 40 copper coins before fleeing. Afterwards, the owner reported the incident to the Caojiadu Branch, requesting that they be pursued and arrested.

Lian Xingteng's Cause of Death Unknown, Internal Examination in Progress 168

Hu Lida Still Detained for Further Interrogation

Lian Xingteng, from Chuansha, Pudong, went to a Westerner's place at 16 Broadway Road at 11:00 AM on the 3rd of this month. Letter 176

Dear Sir, We have seen a news item in your newspaper's local news column entitled "Judge's Persuasion Brings Couple Back Together." After reading it, we found that it differs greatly from the facts. According to the report, Xu Xueshan had an affair, abused and beat his wife, abandoned his young daughter, and forced her to return to her mother's home in Ningbo. None of this is true. It is all one-sided testimony from Xu Xiaomei. Xu Xiaomei's failure to live in her husband's home was her own decision. This time, Xu Xiaomei suddenly applied to the court for divorce mediation, but when she stated the purpose of her application in court, she suddenly changed her request to cohabitation, which is inconsistent. It is believed that discerning people can understand this without saying. Xu Xueshan's original intention was to have the couple cohabit and not divorce. Therefore, our lawyer, representing Xu Xueshan, stated in court that the couple should cohabit, and that Xu Xiaomei's failure to live in her husband's home was her own decision, so there was no need to apply for mediation. Now that she wants to cohabit, it should not be a problem. This is the actual situation. We are afraid that there may be some misunderstanding, so we hereby write to your chief editor to check and make corrections. Sincerely, Lawyer Zhu Yunhui, May 8th.

Old Zhoushan Person Tours New Dinghai 178

— Tingchen

The Zhoushan Islands, isolated overseas east of Zhejiang, the county seat of Dinghai, located on one of the larger islands in the archipelago, is mountainous with little farmland. The rice produced is insufficient to feed the populace for even one season. A small number of wealthy individuals in the city and countryside can afford to eat rice and wear silk, but the majority subsist on buckwheat, vegetable fiber, and other coarse grains. Only the vicinity of the suburbs and the mountain valleys have a small amount of fertile land. Residents are compelled to compete with the mountains for soil, often piling up layers of rocks against the mountain cliffs to create terraced fields to supplement cultivation. However, these yield crops when there is adequate water, but are fruitless in drought. Further up, they cultivate wheat, barley, sweet potatoes, and corn. Still higher, they plant pines, cypresses, and other miscellaneous trees. Those areas unsuitable for trees are left to grow shrubs and wild grasses, providing firewood for cooking. Looking out, the mountain colors are lush and verdant, refreshing the eyes and broadening the mind, as the wilderness expands. Islanders along the coast mostly rely on fishing and salt production for a living. The elderly, weak, women, and children draw seawater, filter it to clarify it, and then sun-dry the brine to make salt, which is then sold to the salt bureau. The strong and able travel overseas by boat to catch sea fish, toiling their entire lives just to make ends meet. Driven by hunger and cold, many residents have no choice but to go north to Hunan or south to Yue (Guangdong and Guangxi), and some even venture to foreign lands, selling their labor and enduring inhumane lives in exchange for meager profits. This has been the general and pervasive state of the livelihood of Dinghai residents in the past. During this trip back to my hometown, although I did not traverse the entire county, I only took a look at the urban and suburban areas and found that many old aspects have changed, refreshing my eyes and ears. I will now record what I have seen and heard, to serve as filler for this newspaper, and to elicit a smile from the readers.

I was born and raised in Dinghai, but have lived elsewhere for over thirty years. Initially, I would return once a year, but now it has been over ten years since I last set foot in my hometown. This time, I accompanied relatives to bring the coffin of Mr. He back for burial, so on the twenty-second of last month, I and my family boarded the Chuanshan steamship, set sail in the evening, and accompanied by Mr. He’s brothers, nephews, and uncle, and my old friend Mr. Zhang Shaogeng. We received preferential treatment from the ship's staff, and the journey was not lonely as we chatted with each other. Mr. Zhang, who has lived in Shenjiamen for generations, is especially knowledgeable about seafood. According to him, at its peak, Dinghai's fishing industry had over 20,000 fishing boats, generating over 8 million yuan in revenue annually. Subsequently, due to the weak purchasing power of the Chinese people, coupled with foreign encroachment, the industry gradually declined over the years. In the past two years, Shanghai and Ningbo financial institutions have tightened credit and are unwilling to recklessly issue loans, resulting in fishing boats remaining idle, unable to set sail for fishing. Shanghai and Ningbo gentry and merchants have repeatedly telegraphed officials in Beijing and Hangzhou to appeal, but no substantive solutions have been forthcoming. This has been reported in the Shenbao. The fishing season has arrived again this year, and the boat owners, compelled by circumstances, have sought other means, scraping together funds from various sources just to barely get out to sea. Therefore, it is foreseeable that their performance will be poor, he said. By morning, the wind was calm and the waves were gentle, with only slight tremors on the Tongsha sea. After a night of peaceful sleep, the ship arrived at Chuanshan Pier at six o'clock. After a brief stop, passengers and cargo were unloaded, and the ship weighed anchor and set sail. At seven-thirty, we arrived at Zhoushan Pier, amidst the clamor of firecrackers, as Mr. He's relatives and friends had been waiting at the pier for the arrival of the coffin. After raising the coffin and temporarily housing the spirit, we took rickshaws from Datoutou towards the South Gate. Dinghai, being located in a remote coastal region, has historically been plagued by pirates. The officials and merchants of the county mostly do not advocate demolishing the city walls. Only after the outer city wall of the South Gate was demolished did we have breakfast at a relative's house. Subsequently, accompanied by Mr. Sun Liqing and his brothers, we visited Dinghai Park. The park is located at the foot of Suoshan Mountain in the west of the city and was rebuilt from the old garrison headquarters, covering an area of over twenty mu. Dinghai Middle School and Dinghai Hospital are also located there. The main hall of the park is the Chengren Shrine, dedicated to the Ming Dynasty Prince Lu and his officials, national heroes who resisted the Qing army. To the side of the shrine gate is a palace well, the site where Prince Lu's consort died for her cause. Next to the well stands a stone stele, engraved with an account of the event. Further inside is a small hall, the four walls covered with hanging scrolls and horizontal inscriptions, recording anecdotes of loyal officials and righteous men of the late Ming Dynasty. Reading them evokes respect and a sense of national consciousness. The aforementioned stone stele, calligraphy, and paintings are all the work of Liqing, a licentiate. When Mr. Huang Renzhi passed through Dinghai, he praised them highly and subsequently established a literary friendship with Mr. Sun before departing. After the visit, we returned to the relative's house for lunch. After a brief rest, we went to Wuyang Mountain in the eastern suburbs to pay respects at my late father's grave. We sat down on the tombstone and chatted with the villagers about agricultural matters. According to them, in recent years, after a year of hard work, they can only scrape together a few dozen yuan in paper money. After household expenses, even one yuan is insufficient. Some even resort to borrowing money at high interest rates. Reflecting on their words, it is clear evidence of agricultural bankruptcy, but the villagers are simple and honest and do not know of such a term. We slowly entered the city and lodged at a relative's house. That day, I was extremely tired, and after dinner, I fell soundly asleep.

Dinghai's construction endeavors have shown improvement since the National Revolutionary Army unified the North and South and Zhejiang had started to show signs of progress. Currently, only running water is yet to be constructed due to the scale of the project. Residents use rainwater and well water for drinking and washing. Otherwise, it can be said that everything is more or less available, albeit on a small scale. Parks, hospitals, and middle schools have already been mentioned. Elementary schools for both boys and girls are scattered around the urban area, and the school buildings are quite presentable. Near the city suburbs, literacy schools have been established in temples to teach those in the countryside who are illiterate. The local newspaper is only the Zhoubao, but unfortunately, I did not go inside to visit, so I do not know its contents in detail. For fire protection, new-style foreign water carts have been purchased and fire brigades have been established in different districts to prevent fires. Due to the lack of running water, large Taiping water tanks are placed in wide areas along the roadside walls, to be used for suction by the fire hoses. However, the water pressure is insufficient and the effectiveness is weak, as evidenced by the fire at the home of a Mr. in Libei on the night of the twenty-fifth, where, despite all efforts to put out the fire, it still spread to over twenty houses. Dinghai, being an island county, previously did not have a telegraph line due to various reasons, so news was not readily available. Since the installation of wireless telegraph communication, official affairs from Beijing and Hangzhou and important news from Shanghai are known on the same day. Telephones and electric lights are common in both urban and rural areas, so news is readily available and the place is brightly lit. However, electric lights are only available at night. Mr. Ma Zukang of the electric company, because Mr. He was involved in initiating the company, had a decorative archway made of electric lights erected at the company's entrance on the day of his funeral, with special daytime electricity provided for decoration. As for the streets, the middle section has been repaved with stone strips, and the sides are connected with cement, but there are no sidewalks. However, because there are no cars, the width and pressure are sufficient to support it. The Tangjiapeng Road and Model Road inside and outside the South Gate are particularly good. The old bridges were all made of stone steps. Now, to facilitate the passage of rickshaws and bicycles, all the bridges in the city and suburbs have been rebuilt as flat bridges to facilitate traffic, but the bridges in the distant suburbs still have stone steps. When a rickshaw reaches the bridge, passengers must get out and wait for the rickshaw to cross the bridge before they can get back on. This is very inconvenient for travelers. In addition, passengers' sleeves are easily scratched by the body of the rickshaw. The cushions are not thick enough, and the springs are uneven, making them uncomfortable for the passengers' buttocks. The rickshaw pullers also need to be trained. The streets in the city are still wide, so there is no danger in driving. Outside the city, the roads become narrower, but the rickshaw pullers bury their heads and rush forward, causing the rickshaw to jolt, lightly injuring the buttocks and even overturning the rickshaw, which is detrimental to both the puller and the passenger. This is something that those in charge of road administration and rickshaw management should pay close attention to. Dinghai is mountainous, and one must often pass through one or two mountain passes to reach a township, which the locals call "crossing the pass." Rickshaws are definitely not suitable for long-distance travel. One must switch to a "sliding chair," as the locals call it. This is the old mode of transportation in Dinghai. The sedan chair bearers are very experienced, so they can safely navigate steep cliffs and dangerous precipices. Water transportation is all by steamship. There are small steamers going to Chuanshan, Zhenhai, Ningbo, Putuo, Daishan, Shenjiamen, and other places every day, and there are direct steamers to Shanghai in the north and Haimen, Wenzhou, and Ruian in the south of the province. The people of this county travel all over the world, which is no doubt due to the convenience of the sea routes.

In the financial sector, banks such as the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Commercial Bank all have small-scale Western-style buildings in Dinghai, establishing branches to absorb deposits and facilitate remittances. Other shops selling foreign goods, groceries, silk fabrics, and cloth are extremely dazzling in order to attract customers, but there is no night market or neon lights. Other shops are roughly similar to those in the interior of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and they are all languishing. As a result, money flows from the countryside to the city, then from the city to the metropolis, and finally from the metropolis to the industrialized countries. It is truly lamentable to speak of this.

The old public institutions included the Dinghai Subprefecture Office, the garrison headquarters, and the new and old academies. Now, the subprefecture office has been converted into the county government, the garrison headquarters has been converted into Dinghai Park, and the academies have been converted into schools. New institutions include the Dinghai District Court and the County Public Security Bureau. There are fifty to sixty police officers on the city's main streets to maintain order and investigate theft. However, due to insufficient funding, they have been merged into the county government and managed by the Public Security Section. The police uniforms are still quite neat. Slogans of the New Life Movement are hung everywhere on wooden signs. The county government has designated poster boards, scattered in important locations in the city and suburbs, so the corners of walls and roofs are kept clean, suggesting the diligence of the cleaning campaign.

Zhejiang Province is now a province where opium has been eradicated, so no opium dens or places for indulging in such vices have been found inside or outside Dinghai city. Gambling is naturally prohibited in public places, but occasional games of mahjong in private homes are not forbidden. Currently, the only problem is public security. The county residents mostly go out to engage in industry and commerce, while people from Wenzhou, Taizhou, and northern Jiangsu flock to live there. It is undeniable that these people are of mixed character. The city streets are safe because of the police, but life in the countryside is difficult, and when people have nothing to eat, they inevitably resort to desperate measures. Robberies and kidnappings occur from time to time, so most villagers with some wealth move to the city for safety. This is a matter that the local authorities must consider in terms of security measures. Dinghai is connected to Japan in the east, to the South Seas in the south, and is the key point of the Qiantang River and the Yangtze River in the northwest. In theory, it should be a national defense fortress, but the country's affairs are numerous and complex, so this is not yet under consideration.

On the twenty-fourth, we escorted the coffin to Xiaoyan Mountain. It rained that day. Although we took rickshaws, we could not cross the Jiong Bridge, so we had to walk. The small paths between the paddy fields were muddy and slippery, so we had to be careful. On the twenty-fifth, I took a boat to Baiquan Township to visit the elders of my maternal family. When I got off the sedan chair, I felt like a stranger who had not changed his accent. When I entered the hall to pay respects, I learned that my eighty-year-old maternal uncle and seventy-year-old maternal aunt had passed away last summer and winter. At the time, I felt regretful that I had not been notified sooner and could not attend their funerals in person. When I saw their remains, I was overcome with sadness, so seeing my cousins filled me with new feelings. On the twenty-sixth, I went to Xiaoyang'ao to pay respects at the ancestral tombs and ancestral shrine. I talked with the villagers again and again and found that they were struggling to make a living. Dinghai County only produces grain, seafood, and salt, which is far from enough to offset the cost of imported goods. If a village becomes a county, a county becomes a province, and a province becomes a country, and a village, a county, and a province all run trade deficits, how can the people not be poor and the country not be weak? Economic aggression, nibbling away at the rice, reaches us living in the cities. How can we not be disheartened when we think of this?

Page 15

Sports News

The Purpose and Hope of Participating in the Olympic Games: Li Huitang, Sent from Hong Kong on May 5th 179

In addition to participating in the World Olympic Games, our national football team will first travel to Java and other places in Southeast Asia to play more than 20 matches. After the Olympic Games, they will travel to various countries to compete. This is an unprecedented undertaking in Chinese football and sports. Football is arguably the most developed sport in our country, so the team's travels and competition details will surely attract the attention of the Chinese people. Mr. Li Huitang, the captain of the Chinese football team, has specially written about his life and competitions along the way in Europe, which will continue to be published in this newspaper. Readers are encouraged to pay attention. First, we have recorded Mr. Li's article "The Purpose and Hope of Participating in the Olympic Games" on the left. (Editor)

This time, the football team is participating in the Summer Olympic Games, and many people who care for us deeply but do not understand the overall situation will invariably hold the same extravagant hope, expecting this group of athletes to bring home the world championship title from the arena of fierce competition in their very first participation. While this is theoretically possible, it is not yet the right time to hope for it. Given the current situation, it is akin to asking us to carry Mount Tai and cross the North Sea. This is not about underestimating ourselves. In fact, in terms of our innate physique, comfortable living, training methods, technical level, and the enthusiasm with which the nation and society promote it, we are not even close to being on par with others.

There are also some people who believe that we are already struggling to compete with the foreigners residing in China, so going to the world football stage would be like a small sorcerer meeting a great one. In today's situation of national crisis and economic hardship, it is not right to waste a huge amount of travel expenses just to embarrass ourselves in front of foreigners. This argument seems to have some valid points at first glance, but if we are already aware of our own immaturity, we should not be complacent and self-satisfied, but should find opportunities to improve. We should not sit idle at home, refusing to eat because of fear of choking, and remain stagnant. Moreover, if our country is to participate in the Olympic Games, football is the most technically impressive sport, which can refresh the foreigners' perspective. Therefore, advocating against sending a team seems to be a narrow view from a well.

As I have repeatedly said, our purpose this time is not to seek a championship. We only know to focus our entire spirit on "effort," bringing out all our true skills and strength without reservation. Our aim is to give foreigners a good impression of us. Our purpose is not limited to participating in the Olympic Games in Berlin. After the Olympic Games, we also want to travel to other countries to learn from them. We want to carefully observe and study their strengths, such as techniques, training methods, and changes in formation, using all our ingenuity to try to understand their subtle points, and to seek knowledge and progress with the excitement of an elementary school student. We want to treat ourselves as a piece of raw iron to be forged, becoming more useful with each strike, so that we will not have made this trip in vain.

Our hope this time is to be able to present our country's thousands of years of Eastern culture and the youthful spirit of the new era at the Summer Olympic Games, where the eyes and ears of the world are gathered, washing away the foreigners' negative perception of China as the "sick man of the East." More importantly, after we return home, we want to use the new knowledge and teaching materials we have absorbed during this long journey to influence the football community in our country by setting an example. We hope to impart the new skills we have learned into the minds of the younger generation. If we are to give up our playing careers, we will also use our identity and qualifications as coaches to guide the younger generation, so that football in our country can make overall and widespread progress, raising the current level to the world standard, so that we will not have made this trip in vain.

At the banquet of the Lixingshe in the capital, the presidents, ministers, and officials expressed their fervent expectations of us, summarized in the eight words "strive to observe" and "adopt strengths and discard weaknesses." This reasonable expectation makes us feel the greatness of our mission and the weight of our responsibility, and we dare not be lazy or neglectful. In my own reply, I also said that what our sports community needs now is not just a few dozen or a few hundred excellent players. Fundamentally speaking, there are very few outstanding individuals among China's 400 million people. The elite selected from 400 million people can sometimes not even defeat a battalion of foreign soldiers. Even if they win, there is not much glory in it. This is because in recent years, we have only achieved a distorted development, and we have not done any practical work in the widespread aspects. How can we blame it? Therefore, what we feel we need is the universal progress of the whole country, to make all 400 million compatriots athletic and to understand the fundamental meaning of sports. At that time, why worry that China will suffer foreign aggression?

In short, in addition to the responsibilities of striving to observe and strive to express Eastern civilization during this trip abroad to participate in the Olympic Games, the greatest and most important work lies in the future after returning home.

The accommodation problem for athletes from each district must be reported to the committee in writing for unified arrangement.
