The French Boxer Indemnity Funds for Sino-French Education and Charity 196

The French return of the Boxer Indemnity funds began with the exchange of notes between China and France in June of the eleventh year of the Republic of China. An agreement between China and France was reached in April of the fourteenth year, stipulating that a certain amount of US dollar bonds from the Boxer Indemnity would be used annually as subsidies for Sino-French education and charity. A Sino-French Education Fund Committee was jointly established by both parties in April of the fourteenth year as an independent entity. (The current Chinese delegation includes Li Shuhua, Liu Xichang, Chen Jianxiao, Luo Jialun, Li Yuying, Zou Lu, Shen Yinmo, Zhang Gongquan, Zhou Zuomin, Qian Yongming, and Liu Fucheng, among others. The French delegation includes Wei Lide, He Bo, Zhu Hande, and Baertake.) A Fund Management Committee was organized within the committee (currently including Bar, Masu, Handerwei, Zhang Gongquan, and Zhou Zuomin), with members planning and preparing. Although the current accumulated funds are small, if the unpaid portion of the French Boxer Indemnity interest-free bonds is entrusted to the committee for safekeeping, the face value would be 175.8 million francs, a significant amount, and development would be substantial. Recently, the fund committee established five special representatives (including Zhang Gongquan) to handle special affairs and negotiate with the Chinese and French governments on the Sino-French Education Fund issue. The Sino-French Education Fund Committee's activities include self-operated projects and subsidies to other organizations, focusing on education and culture, mainly in the following areas: A. Completing the only educational institution between China and France, the most important of which is the Sino-French University. B. Subsidizing effective Sino-French academic institutions or schools at home and abroad, such as the Shanghai Xujiahui Observatory, the Lyon Sino-French Institute, Aurora University in Shanghai, the Sino-French National College, and the Tianjin Industry and Commerce College, which receive annual subsidies. C. In accordance with the Sino-French refund agreement, funds allocated for Sino-French education are also used for Sino-French charitable purposes. Therefore, current recipients of the committee's subsidies include Sino-French hospitals in Beiping, Guangdong, Yunnan, Guiyang, and Longzhou. D. Subsidizing students studying in France, limited to those who have entered the school and achieved excellent results as certified by the school. Currently, the committee subsidizes 11 students with full scholarships, 4 students with partial or small scholarships, and 2 students with special research grants. In addition, one graduate of the French Department of Peking University is specially awarded a scholarship to study in France each year. As of the end of last year, 4 students have been selected. E. The committee also cooperates with other organizations or Boxer Indemnity agencies to subsidize other cultural undertakings, including: 1. Subsidizing the construction of a vault for the Palace Museum; 2. Subsidizing the construction of the Lu Mo Ke Hall in the garden of the Natural History Museum for the research laboratories and specimen rooms of the Beiping Research Institute's physiology, zoology, and botany departments; 3. Subsidizing the National Beiping Library's purchase of useful French books and exchanging librarians with the Paris Library; 4. Subsidizing the Ministry of Education's National Language Unification Committee to compile a Sino-French dictionary; 5. Subsidizing the Construction Committee's dispatch of personnel to France for practical study; 6. Subsidizing Dr. Zhao Chengzhang's research on Chinese medicine; 7. Subsidizing the Radium Research Institute, etc. C. Establishing the Sino-French Cultural Exchange and Publication Committee (members include Shen Yinmo, Li Yuying, Li Shuhua, Liu Xichang, and Duo Ermeng). This committee is the only self-operated project of the Sino-French Education Fund Committee. The purpose of establishing this committee is to mutually translate and publish works so that the academic thoughts of the two countries can be effectively communicated and a plan for exchanging publications can be formulated and implemented systematically. In addition, inviting famous French scholars such as Bo Xihe, La Luo, Fa Ye, and Heber to give lectures in China is also one of the Sino-French cultural affairs handled by the committee. As for participating in the construction of a dormitory for Chinese students studying in France in the University Village in Paris, it is only being planned and implemented by the committee, as the funding has not yet been fully realized. The total amount of the Boxer Indemnity returned is 391,581,529 francs and 050 centimes, which is equivalent to US$75,556,964.457, based on the exchange rate of one US dollar for 5.1826 francs. The funds are gradually advanced and lent to the Sino-French Industrial Bank as the fund for the bank to issue 5% US dollar bonds. The purpose is to: 1. Exchange for interest-free bonds held by foreign creditors; 2. Handle Sino-French education and charity; 3. Pay off the remaining unpaid capital owed by the Chinese government; 4. Allocate funds to repay various debts owed by the Chinese government to the bank. Regarding the second item, at least US$200,000 to US$250,000 is allocated each year. It is reported that the distribution method is to leave a small portion as a fund and use almost all of it for Sino-French education, culture, and charity. The fixed income each year after that will be US$250,000, and the amount of unfixed income will vary each year until the year 36 of the Republic of China, when the debt will be fully repaid.

Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan Chen Cipuo Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 197

Talks About Japanese Education Being on Track

Will Visit Education Minister Wang in Beijing Tomorrow to Report

Chen Cipuo, the supervisor of the Office of Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan, arrived in Shanghai on the Shanghai Maru at 3:00 PM yesterday after being recalled to China by Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education. He immediately retired to a hotel to rest and will go to Beijing on the 10th to visit Minister Wang, report on the current situation of students studying in Japan and the affairs of the office, and request instructions on future directions. He will stay in the country for about a month before returning to his post. A reporter from the Central News Agency met with Supervisor Chen at the hotel. The following is a record of the conversation about the current situation of students studying in Japan and recent political developments in Japan.

Japanese Education is on Track

Mr. Chen first stated that he was dispatched to manage affairs related to studying in Japan last August and it will soon be nine months. This time, he was ordered to return to the country to report and will not stay in Shanghai for long before going to Beijing to visit Minister Wang and report on everything. Since his arrival, with the concerted efforts of his colleagues, hard work, and the guidance and assistance of various parties at home and abroad, Japanese education has been put on track. This is something that can be reported to the people of the country with comfort. However, active work still awaits future efforts, so he will make some requests when he visits the Minister of Education this time to be able to follow them.

Hope that Japan will not Indiscriminately Accept Students

Mr. Chen continued, "When I was in Japan, in order to ensure that Chinese students studying in Japan could enrich their academic abilities under strict education and training so that they could serve the country in the future, I specifically visited important members of the Japanese Ministry of Education and the Cultural Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as well as the authorities of various universities, hoping that the Japanese education authorities would not indiscriminately accept Chinese students. For Chinese students, this would not only prevent them from gaining practical benefits and cause them great losses, but also greatly affect the credibility of Japanese schools. Therefore, the Japanese education authorities have been able to understand our country's painstaking efforts to ensure the practical learning of students studying abroad and have agreed to help correct the past malpractices. This is indeed something that can be reported to the people of the country with comfort."

Unified Introduction Has Been Recognized by Japan

Mr. Chen further stated that the Office of Supervisor is now responsible for the unified introduction of students to schools. Japanese schools have refused to admit students who do not have an introduction letter from the Office of Supervisor. At the same time, the Office of Supervisor not only detains the documents of those who forge documents but also escorts them back to the country. Even if the authorities of domestic schools obtain certificates through personal relationships and deceive their way into identification, their student status must be revoked once verified. Currently, there are approximately 5,000 students registered with the Office of Supervisor in Japan.

Hope that Students Will Not Try to Be Lucky

In the past, among students studying abroad, there were often those who were not familiar with Japanese, or even those who had never been to Japan but only entrusted friends in Japan to register. This situation is certainly not right. Now, the Office of Supervisor will not issue an introduction letter to students studying in Japan without verifying their photos and conducting a serious assessment. However, the general students in the country often still do not understand the government's intention to rectify the study abroad business and go abroad casually, which causes them great losses. This malpractice is mostly due to students' lack of legal spirit and their neglect of practical learning. In the future, students should absolutely correct this wrong notion and think about their own studies and the future of the country and nation. However, it is still hoped that the press can convey this information at any time and arouse the attention of all parties.

Zhejiang University Establishes Publicly Funded Students 198

Starting in the 25th Year, the Quota is 5%

Since the new president of Zhejiang University, Zhu Kezhen, took office, he has appointed deans, reorganized equipment, and the entire school has been refreshed. Under the guidance of the new president, students have been able to focus on their studies, and the school, which had been in turmoil for half a year, has gradually returned to normal. President Zhu, in view of the depletion of the social economy and the pity of the poor and out-of-school children, has decided to establish publicly funded student quotas from the second half of the year. Those who are admitted will be completely free of charge, so that children from poor families will have the opportunity to receive higher education. In his first speech to the students after taking office, Zhu repeatedly stated the importance of publicly funded students. In the past, under the imperial examination system, children from poor families could still strive to study hard and achieve success, but today, higher education is almost exclusively enjoyed by children from middle-class families and above. It is already very difficult for middle-class families to provide their children with high school education, and as for university students, 300 to 400 yuan per year is not enough. Even in Jiangsu, which is the most prosperous province in the country, according to statistics, 66% of residents have an annual income of less than 90 yuan. Zhejiang may not be as good as this number, so children who cannot enjoy higher education due to economic reasons actually account for more than 99% of the total population. It is very regrettable to bury talents. Now that the university has established this publicly funded student system, it is of great significance to society. It is reported that the plan has been submitted to the Ministry of Education for review and implementation. The original text is as follows:

Measures for the National Zhejiang University to Recruit Publicly Funded Students: 1. Applicants for publicly funded students must have a certificate from the graduating school to prove that their families are indeed impoverished and cannot afford university education expenses. 2. The ranking of the students who apply for publicly funded students must be within one-sixth of all admitted students in order to be admitted (for example, if the total number of admitted students is 60, the ranking of publicly funded students must be within the top 10). 3. Applicants for publicly funded students who fail cannot be admitted as ordinary fee-paying students. 4. The quota for publicly funded students at all levels shall not exceed 5% of the number of students at that level. 5. Students who pass the examination for publicly funded students will be given a subsidy of 250 yuan per year by the school, divided into two installments, which will be paid at the beginning of each semester, but all fees that should be paid according to school regulations will be deducted from this subsidy. 6. Those whose average grade point average in the semester is below one-third of the best students in the same grade of their college will have their publicly funded student status revoked. 7. The period for which publicly funded students receive subsidies shall not exceed four years.

Seafood: Kelp Inventory is Low and Sales are Also Slow 225

The Market Situation is Still Stable; the Season for New Product Offerings is No Longer Close

Kelp, also known as haicao, comes from Japan and is produced in Hokkaido and in all coastal regions. The types are too numerous to count. Tenkachi, Ogoku, Horoizumi, Nemuro, Hamanaka are the best quality; the next best are Kunashiri, Akkeshi, Kawaji, Onne Village, and Shoucho; the next best are snake skin, two honors, Sanban, Jittai, Nekoashi, and Tekizoku. Beside the quality classes, there are also the harvest types of Fukuuke, Kakaeuke, and Akizuke. The new supplies usually come on stage at the summer solstice and stop at the end of autumn and start of winter. It was first imported to our country around the early years of the Qing Emperor Guangxu, and it has been sixty+ years since then. The sales market was initially limited to the northern provinces and then it gradually extended to sales in each city in the Yangtze River region. Because the prices were low and the taste was appropriate, the people were happy to purchase it. The highest amount of yearly imports totalled six to seven hundred thousand dan and the lowest was three to four hundred thousand dan. But in recent years, purchasing power has been weak because of the bankruptcy of rural areas in the country. Moreover, the production of each area isn't as good as it was in the past, so last year's rice product totalled 200,000+ dan which is less than half of the strongest years. Because the sales from each road aren't as good as in the past, sales are quite able to support stocks even though supplies are low. In the current market, Nemuro -Enchu- Fukuuke Harvests cost 9 yuan and the Akiuke Harvest is 8.8 yuan. Akkeshi -Kawaji- Kunashiri etc. - Fukuuke Harvests cost 8.6 yuan and the Akiuke Harvest is 8.3-8.4 yuan. Shoucho costs 8.2 yuan, Nekoashi costs 6.5 yuan, Nibantai costs 6.2 yuan, and Sanban costs 5.7-5.8 yuan. The other inferior goods have no market because supplies have ended. The prosperity of the market in the future must be decided by good harvest of the new supplies and the strength of each shop's sales road.

Page 17

Shenbao Women's Section

Sincerely Celebrate with "My Mother Special Page"

Today, on Mother's Day, we send blessings to all mothers around the world and pay sincere respect to my mother (Zhou Shoujuan) who has endured hardship for 36 years.

My Mother 231

— Zhu Ying, National Chinan University

Twenty years ago, being a daughter-in-law was not easy. My mother, unable to endure her husband's abuse and her in-laws' scolding, escaped from that prison-like large family, carrying a baby girl—me—on her back.

A daughter-in-law running away, coming from a family of scholars for generations, was truly a disgrace. Therefore, her husband's family naturally wouldn't tolerate it, and our maternal grandparents, because of her unfilial return, disowned this shameful daughter. They only allocated some land and houses barely enough to sustain life. The mother and daughter lived a lonely life amidst cold ridicule and heated criticism.

Twenty years passed like a gentle spring breeze, fleeting away, disappearing. The lingering images of the disgraceful (?) event in people's minds had long faded and been forgotten. Even the father who gave birth to me reportedly died the year before last. As for me? Through my mother's skillful weaving and a difficult life, I finally completed secondary education and entered the gates of higher learning. But when I think of my mother's hardships, enduring twenty years as if it were a single day, how sad it is!

My mother often said, "If it weren't for you, I would have died long ago. For you, I have lived until now, enduring humiliation and suffering." I know that although I am already over twenty years old, my mother has suffered enough. The wrinkles on her face are deep, and her hair is white. It truly makes me afraid to gaze at her!

Mother! From the distant Shanghai shore, I wish you good health, peace, and happiness!

My Mother 232

— Wang Dongming, Songjiang Girls' High School

My mother is a very ordinary woman, seemingly without anything worthy of praise. But her greatness lies in this, because she has done her best silently, enabling my father to achieve great success in his scholarship, and enabling each of us siblings to become established.

My maternal grandfather was a licentiate of the former Qing Dynasty, with very strict family teachings, but his speech was very humorous. My mother was greatly influenced by my maternal grandfather, often joking, but possessing a dignity that made people not dare to approach her. My mother did not study as a child. After marrying into our family, she gradually learned to read ordinary letters, and later she could even write family letters.

I mentioned earlier that my mother's greatness does not lie in any great career she pursued herself. Her greatness lies precisely in handling household affairs, which modern women disdain to do. My mother was only twenty-one or twenty-two years old when she got married, but because she was my father's second wife, she became the mother of three children. Fortunately, my elder brothers all had the temperament of boys, easygoing and gentle, and treated my mother like their own.

When my mother first came, our family moved to Beiping. We never had any relatives or old friends in Beiping. At that time, my father was either busy all day or reading books at home behind closed doors. All the household affairs were managed by my mother. My mother was so young, yet she had to take care of a family with three children. It was truly not an easy task. My father was helped by my mother, allowing him to feel unburdened by family responsibilities and devote himself to scholarship. This was a major reason for his future achievements.

In the first year of the Republic of China, our family lived in Japan. That was arguably the most difficult time for our family financially. Although my father had some work to do, he also had to study, so it was always difficult to make ends meet. My mother also had another child—my fourth elder brother. Except for an old nanny brought from China, there was no one else to help with everything. Every item of clothing and socks for everyone from my father to the children was made by my mother herself, often working late into the night.

After we returned from Japan, we also lived in Shanghai. Later, my father went to Beiping, and the whole family moved there. While my father was teaching at Tsinghua Research Institute, he suddenly committed suicide at the Summer Palace. My mother was so saddened at that time that she almost didn't want to live. But for the sake of our seven children, she finally resolved to endure hardship and raise us, bringing us back to our hometown.

Everyone knows that my father left no money behind. Fortunately, my eldest brother was already able to be independent, and my mother tried every possible way to ensure that we all received education above the high school level. She often looked at my elder brothers as they became established, smiling through her tears. Now my youngest brother is already in the second year of high school, and all of us siblings know how hard-won the opportunity to study is, and how much effort our mother has put in, so we are able to study hard. Our grades in school often bring my mother a little more joy.

My mother is old now. She no longer has the energetic spirit she once had. This is due to the worries and sorrows she has suffered in the past ten years. But my mother's contribution to society is immortal.

My Mother 233

— Lucy, South Road Women's Normal School

My maternal grandfather was terrifyingly poor. He had two sons and a daughter. When his sons grew up, he also took his daughter and left that broken home. My maternal grandmother relied on the few coins her eldest son earned in the dyehouse to make a living, and she also had to set aside some money for her youngest son to study in private school. Every time she held her rice bowl, she thought of her runaway husband and daughter.

My maternal grandfather wandered in the Jiangnan region; at the same time, his daughter also encountered someone who saved her. This was a wealthy philanthropist in Yiwu, who was also my father.

My father's original family was a complex one, also a large clan. He had married a wife before, and the children she bore were already grown up, and all had married.

This clearly proves my father's age. He was more than twenty years older than my mother. After my mother entered the family, no one sympathized with or comforted her except my father. She endured for the sake of life, for the sake of emotion. In that large family at that time, a large number of slaves were kept. They similarly looked down on my mother, not thinking of themselves.

My father left early and returned late, working outside, so the time he spent with my mother was very little. Thus, my mother's grief deepened day by day. She was often melancholic, taciturn, staring blankly in concentration.

My mother continued to give birth to my elder brother, elder sister, and me amidst a situation of being besieged on all sides. At that time, how she longed for these children to grow up, to gain some solace in life! But when these children had not yet understood the pain of life, they still had to be naughty, causing my mother more pain, and she wept alone.

At that time, not only did my mother not have freedom, we also had no freedom; especially me. I could not win anyone's favor and was often beaten severely by the slaves. Therefore, in my childhood, I was pitifully thin and pale.

We grew up amidst bitter winds and rain.

My father remarried, lived outside, and also had two sons. My mother became extraordinarily depressed, growing inwardly.

One summer, a hot summer, the viewing ornaments deteriorated due to age, the salt yellowed and failed, family affairs declined; and all the erosions of life led to death. My mother looked at these three orphans, her tears streaming down, gradually growing thin. At that time, I was twelve, my sister was fourteen, and my brother was sixteen.

'The spirit is thinner than the autumn clouds.' The door and courtyard were so quiet that they were like an ancient temple. A group of people carrying [the coffin] walked slowly in front of the street, and the footprints of people who had been there had been obliterated. My mother clenched her fists, pacing back and forth.

She could not get the only living expenses. The economic power of the family was still controlled by others. They were so careful that they would not let even a speck of money slip through their fingers. At this time, no one could understand her, except her children. She bit her lip tightly and sold all her jewelry. Ah! She was startled that she was a woman, a widow, in her forties. She still had to wrestle with her living environment.

Her struggles, her endeavors, led us onto the broad, correct path. Therefore, in recent years, my brother has had a career, and my sister has also become a teacher. Only I continue to study.

In my mother's white hair and wrinkles, the light of hope and happiness is revealed. She said: "I am approaching old age. I hope you young children will move forward! Do not let go, do not be discouraged. Because you have become aware of the darkness, you will pursue the light; the light will also illuminate everything about you. May you always remember my words!"

We looked at the distant sky, smiling and shedding tears.

My Mother 234

— Lin Bin, Shanghai Yunzhong Girls' School

Hair streaked with snow, a very high nose, a long, square face, imprinted with wrinkles born of labor, a dimple almost erased by wrinkles, a pair of eyes with deep emotion and love—this is the outline of my mother.

A county along the Qiantang River is the place where my mother was born.

My mother is a woman in her fifties. When she was young, she was bound by the feudal barriers of that time, which deprived her of the opportunity to learn to read. Therefore, she was a blind person with open eyes. She struggled and strove, seeking a glimmer of hope to [missing text] one [missing text] of being literate. The thousands of years of feudal [missing text] covered her eyes, and thousands of years of [missing text] women's [missing text] bound her hands and feet. She could not see the light, she could not explain [missing text] and struggled. All she could do was groan without illness in the powerful, feudal, autocratic prison [missing text] with women who suffered the same fate.

Although my mother's father and mother were people of the previous century, they tried their best to give a little light to their beloved daughter in a dim and harsh environment, but the result was the same: they were subjected to pointing fingers. They watched their daughter bury her desire for knowledge for the sake of dark feudalism.

Later, my mother got married. She managed the family diligently, trying to make a family in a time of transition between the old and new very peaceful, pure, and happy. She cooked meals, sewed clothes, and in her spare time, she asked me to tell her about national affairs. Sometimes I would pout and refuse to read the newspaper or tell her about it. She would then stroke my head with her maternal hand and say, "Child, you must pity your mother. She had no opportunity to study when she was young, so now she is illiterate, cannot read the newspaper, and cannot directly serve the country. In the future, you must use what you can do to help people who cannot do things. Do you understand, child?" Her voice was full of sadness, and my eyes were filled with tears of regret.

Although my mother herself had never studied, when I came home from school, after a certain period of rest, she would urge me to review my studies. She said, "Studying hard is like building yourself firmly. There is your own shadow shaking in the books!" I trusted my mother's words very much, so I worked hard to build myself and find my shadow in the books.

I entered this world with the heart my mother gave me—but not long ago, my mother left me forever. On her deathbed, she said to me, "Child, you are not my exclusive daughter. I have given you to humanity. You are the daughter of humanity. You must work hard for humanity, you must sacrifice for humanity!" My mother loved me very much. There was no pretense, deception, or hypocrisy in her love. All there was was light, warmth, and greatness. Although my mother has left me forever, she did not take her love from my heart! This kind of love overflows in my body and will need me to release it in the future. I want to take my mother's love to love humanity—I am the daughter of humanity—because mother's love is not [missing text] occupied by one person. It [missing text] should [missing text] be scattered, it should shine like the sunlight, so that there will not be a single person in the world who is abandoned without love!

My mother lived her life like this. She has now passed away, but her love continues to grow!—Because nothing can extinguish the love of mothers in the world!

On Mother's Day, bless the health of mothers! Bless all those who have mothers!—Because I am a child without a mother! But, orphans without mothers, let us all call out "Mother" in unison!

My Mother 235

— Shen Yuzhen, Hangzhou Provincial Midwifery School

My mother and I have not seen each other for only a little over two months, but I feel that the time of a little over two months is too long for me. For over two months, in this traveler's land, in this foreign land with no relatives, a traveler's heart is always missing my elderly mother. Especially in this spring day when the cuckoo's calls echo through the wilderness, it deeply touches my lost Han [Chinese] heart. I can't wait to immediately return to my mother's side, throw myself into her gentle [arms], and be stroked by her warm hands.

My mother occupies my entire heart. Sometimes, although I also love books, I never have the passion to love my mother. In fact, my mother is the only one who loves me, so the one I love most is also my mother. After class, on moonlit nights with silver light pouring down, I remember my mother. Isn't this round, white plate my mother's round face? On fragrant mornings, I also think of my mother. Aren't these petals my mother's beautiful smile? In short, everything that I love, I consider to be an epitome of my mother's life.

The spring is bright, the birds are singing, and I am immersed in memories of the past. This is something that happened eight years ago; I returned from night school and caught a pair of little sparrows to play with. A [thin rope] was tightly [tied] on [a sparrow's] foot, and I almost killed it by playing with it. Carelessly, my mother saw it, which resonated with her heartstrings and evoked great emotions. Her eyes suddenly filled with crystal tears, "Zhen'er; do you love Mom?" I was holding the rope in my hand and said in surprise to my mother, "Mom, I love you, I love Mom the most!" My mother stroked my hair and said, "Are you willing to leave your mom?" "No, I will never leave Mom; Mom, what's wrong with your eyes?" I was holding the rope in one hand and immediately grabbed the corner of my mother's clothes with the other. "Zhen'er! Think about it, does this bird have a mom?" I cried; I suddenly threw myself into my mother's arms and burst into loud sobs...

Sparrows are playing spring tunes on the branches. They are enjoying the happiness of family, but I am in this traveler's land, in this foreign land with no relatives, alone immersed in memories of the past, longing for my mother.

My Mother 236

— Yang Shujuan, Great China University

My father died when I was eleven years old. At that time, our family consisted of an elderly grandmother, three younger siblings than me, and my eldest sister, who was only one year older than me. We did not understand any worldly affairs, and only knew to surround our mother, guarding before my father's spirit, weeping. The situation at that time, even thinking about it now, is still very sad.

After my father died, the local bullies often took the opportunity to bully us, writing what donations, and we were assigned more than others. My mother had no choice but to mediate and run around at the doors of these powerful people, often having to see their unjust faces; but my mother never brought back even a hint of anger for us to see.

From my mother's conversation, we knew that my maternal grandmother gave my mother a completely typical education of a virtuous wife and good mother; and my mother herself was even more fully aware that she was a responsible person in society, so my mother felt a great interest in all social issues. My mother did not advocate keeping maids, saying, "It is the most inhumane thing to separate other people's families."

My mother managed the household, imbuing dignity with kindness. My mother never loudly scolded anyone, but everyone had a sense of respect and love for her. Therefore, not only was our family well-organized, but also harmonious and cheerful.

When my father was alive, he was of a chivalrous nature, often helping friends generously, not hesitating to spend a thousand gold. After my father died, debts piled up, and creditors filled the door. My mother had to raise money to repay old debts, support household expenses, and also consider our tuition, so that we would not drop out of school; but my mother often said to us: "I send you to school, not hoping that you will earn money. Studying is about understanding principles. As long as you can serve society in the future and be a complete person, my responsibility will be fulfilled."

When I was about to leave, my mother also said to me: "It is very painful for people who cannot read. After you obtain knowledge yourself, do not forget these people who do not have the opportunity to study." This clearly told me not to study only for myself.

In our hometown, few women can receive education. My mother resolutely sent us sisters to school under that stubborn feudal force, all the way to the present—university.

It has been two years since I came out, and I have not yet returned to see my mother. I don't know how much white hair and wrinkles this heavy economic burden has added to my mother.

My Mother 237

— Jin Yu, Graduate of Anhui University

A purer love than a mother's cannot be found; a scene more meaningful than a child surrounding a mother cannot be found either.

Yes, "My father is the best father in the world, my mother is the best mother in the world." I have seen these two sentences somewhere.

My home is in a village ten miles away from Xiuning County, Anhui Province. There are verdant mountains, lush trees, a small stone bridge, and flowing water in the clear stream below. When the weather is fine, just stand in a place in the village where the view is unobstructed, and you can see the peaks of Huangshan Mountain vaguely between the clouds and sky hundreds of miles away. This is a poetic environment. Before the Taiping Rebellion, the villagers lived and worked in peace and contentment, as if it were a paradise. After the Taiping Rebellion, I heard that my great-grandfather started to pass down farming and reading, maintaining a frugal family style, but life was difficult. My grandfather was a scholar. He treated people and things with a rigorous scholarly nature. My father was raised as a scholar by my grandfather's order.

When my mother came to my house, my great-grandmother and grandparents were still alive. My grandfather was an official traveling in the north, and the family affairs were managed by my great-grandmother. She was a virtuous daughter-in-law serving two generations of elders. My father passed the imperial examination at the prefecture level at the age of nineteen, but did not have money to spend to come home. My mother gave her "greeting gift" as a bride to someone to take to my father to use, because she wanted to commemorate her maternal grandparents, she did not take jewelry to exchange for it. At the same time, in this year, my eldest sister was born, and the following year, my second sister was born. At this time, my father was teaching at the Fengtian Higher School. A year later, he returned to his hometown to say goodbye to his family before going to study in the Americas. At that time, everyone thought that my mother would come out to obstruct him, but it was not so. In addition to giving my father the money that she and her sisters had saved over the years, she also [strengthened] my father's courage to study abroad. From then on, for seven years, my great-grandfather and grandfather died one after another. My mother served my grandmother above, and supported my eldest and second sisters below. In a not-so-rich family, she worked hard to keep my grandmother happy, and my eldest and second sisters both entered school, and did not lack anything.

When my father returned to China, he took my grandmother's whole family to Shanghai. My mother was exactly thirty years old. This was the beginning of my mother's managing the family. In the three years that followed, although I and my younger brother were born, she managed the family strictly. In addition to assigning the duties of the servants, she mostly personally directed and handled things. When we sisters grew up, in addition to urging us to study at any time, she also taught each of us to learn part of the housework. Whether the family was well-off or poor, my family was always a clean and orderly family that made people feel good. Although my mother was strict, she was also very kind. She treated her children and servants with kindness and harmony, unless there was a major mistake. When we were sick or when we were leaving home to go to school, she would personally pack our luggage for us. What the old woman thought of and did was always before us. My mother does not play cards or smoke. Her hobby is flowers and plants. She would not waste the money her father earned with his blood and sweat, but when she used money, she made her husband, children, relatives, and friends feel comfortable, and the poor people received real benefits. It was four years ago, right? My father was wrongly accused in office and was imprisoned for almost a year. My mother exchanged her exquisite jewelry for the tuition for me and my younger brother to enter university, and always earnestly instructed me and my younger brother on how to be extraordinary children.

My mother grew up under the old [education]. She is filial to her parents-in-law, she loves her husband and children, and she can love anyone. Now she is a woman of fifty-four years old. She cannot give speeches, cannot go to dance halls, cannot go to restaurants every day, cannot run schools,... but she will always be the beloved daughter of my maternal grandparents, the virtuous wife of my father, the good mother of us sisters! Good mother, blessings to you!

My Mother 238

— Jia Qiurui, Wuben Girls' Middle School

A round face, a plump figure, and a generous way of treating people—this is my mother. Her surname is Lei, and her given name is Yimei. She was born in Jingzhou, Gansu Province. Her family was not very wealthy. My father said, "She entered the Jia family's door when she was nineteen years old."

When the east turns white, she gets up to cook porridge and handle all the household affairs, such as sweeping the floor! Washing clothes! Buying groceries! Doing needlework! She does everything herself. Although she labors like a panting ox, she has never been sick, nor has she ever uttered a complaint? This is the first special feature of her managing the family.

The second special feature of her managing the family is managing her children, not allowing us to be infected with bad habits and customs, such as smoking, alcohol, and gambling. Every night, she forcibly requires us to review our homework for two hours. On holidays, she does not allow us to play alone, but leads us to play, fearing that we will learn the habits of naughty children.

She is very capable in doing things. One thing can illustrate it. Once, my father suffered from a very serious pinkeye. Although various eye drops were used to treat it, it could not be cured. Later, she thought of an old method from a doctor, which was to lick it with her tongue, and it was finally cured.

Every year in the summer, a group of coolies come to my house to ask my mother for medicines to prevent epidemics and relieve heatstroke (such as Shayaoshui medicine tea, etc.). She always tries her best to supply them. In the severe winter, she printed two hundred rice tickets and bought eighty sets of clothes to give to the extremely poor people. She has been doing this kind of "charitable" thing for five years.

My mother has also done a lot for the good deeds of society. In addition to donating money for relief, she always tries her best to help orphans who have no home to return to. Therefore, people living near my house say that my mother is a blessed grandchild.

The above is my mother's background, management of the family, and contribution to society!

My Mother 239

— Wang Renhui, Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School

My mother was my maternal grandmother's first daughter. She was a young lady in a large family, but because there were many people, her mother favored sons over daughters and didn't love her very much. Only her grandmother truly protected her. She hired a teacher especially for her to teach her to read. From then on, she lived with her grandmother. She worked hard at her studies, and her life was happy and blessed. She married at the age of ten, and a year later, she gave birth to my older brother, and then she gave birth to me. In the third month of the year after I was born in October, my father unfortunately passed away! My twenty-four-year-old mother became a widow.

Poor mother, seeing us two siblings, one three years old and the other one year old, how could she not be filled with anxiety! The love she had for us was indescribable. I remember when I was eight years old, my older brother fell ill. How worried my mother was at that time! She couldn't eat in peace during the day! She couldn't sleep peacefully at night! She didn't feel fatigue and always maintained her spirits, earnestly hoping that my brother would get rid of the sickness as soon as possible. My kind mother was very religious. For the sake of her children, she ate vegetarian food for three months of the year in the first, fifth, and ninth months. When we were studying, she sat beside us to supervise. Alas! She tasted all kinds of hardships for our sakes.

My mother was extremely simple and frugal. The household equipment was very simple and clean. She had considerable artistic skills. She handled all the income and expenditure accounts by herself. Even a penny was taken very seriously. Although no one in my family earns money now, our siblings' education and the family's expenses do not require borrowing from outside. Our family is very modern. It is really fun and happy. Everything we enjoy is managed by my mother for us.

My home is in a not-so-developed countryside. Everything is very isolated. As for education, there is even less to mention. When my grandfather saw this situation, he started a primary school in the countryside. My mother has been working at the school ever since, for more than ten years now. Her benevolent heart extends to the general public. Everyone in my hometown praises her ability to handle affairs. I have such a mother, and I am really the happiest person in the world, but how can I repay my mother's deep kindness!

How Can There Be Compassion in the World? 250

— Bored

The Italian army entered A-jing on May 5th. The modern tragedy reached its final act. The A-people fought hard for seven months, and the matter was finally over, becoming Italy's sacrifice. However, according to the telegram from A-jing on the 5th, the entire city of A-jing was on fire, thick smoke billowed everywhere, and mobs roamed everywhere looting. People in A-jing were eagerly awaiting the arrival of the Italian army. However, the Italian army did not want to be accused of occupying A-jing by force, so they did not rush to enter. Only when the A-jing delegation went to the Italian army to hand over the capital did the Italian army enter. This clearly shows that Italy forcibly occupied A-guo, but refused to take the name of forcible occupation. In this way, A-guo's demise was not Italy's forcible occupation, but rather A-guo itself not wanting its country and offering A-guo to Italy entirely. Is this deceiving someone or deceiving heaven? The tragedy of national subjugation is so incredible.

When the A-king left the capital, important leaders of A-guo, such as General Gustai and General Gasa, sat in the reception room of the Governor's Palace. The A-queen and her children stayed in the private room. When the A-king left the Governor's Palace, he walked down the steps shoulder to shoulder with the queen, and the children followed behind. General Gasa and others stood on both sides. When the A-king and queen passed in front of them, they all bowed to the ground. Everyone was silent at the time, and the scene was very sad. The A-king suffered such a tragedy of national subjugation, and the A-people tasted the feeling of national subjugation. This was originally a very painful and heartbreaking period. However, at that time, there were two news reporters who, because the Italian army had not yet entered the capital, took the opportunity to hold a wedding at the British Embassy. The groom was the Times reporter, Steel, and the bride was the Spanish Ms. Hariros, a special reporter for the French newspaper. When the ceremony was held, the sound of gunfire from the mobs outside the embassy was like a string of pearls. Therefore, some newspapers called it a good story at the time of the subjugation of Abyssinia. Even from the perspective of the news reporter, it was a good story. They are losing their country, and we are getting married. What does it have to do with each other? But what kind of impression does it leave on the local people? Therefore, I say that there is no compassion in the world.

When the Italian army was approaching A-jing, Mussolini still ordered a test of public mobilization, announcing this decision in the House of Representatives. Representatives of the diplomatic corps, senior military officers from the army, navy, and air force were present. First, Count Chiano gave the opening speech. His first words were, "The A-king has fled." Then the entire house cheered, and the sound shook the roof. The parliament then adjourned for an hour to express its joy at the turning point in the A-guo war. Naturally, Italy had achieved its goal of occupying A-guo by force, so how could it not be joyous? The other day, the British cabinet held a meeting to study the issue of the A-king's departure and decided on the steps that the British government had taken regarding this matter. However, according to semi-official sources, the sanctions ultimately failed. Since this has been proven to be true, Britain does not intend to persist in its sanctions policy in the future. Some people in the political circles also said that the League of Nations must be reformed in the future, because the League of Nations' prestige has been swept away. In the A-Italy war, Britain helped A-guo a lot, but it was also fruitless. At this point, it can only say a few passive idle words. Even if there is compassion but no compassionate power, it can only be in vain.

After Watching "Wet Paint" 251

— Li Yi

The China Traveling Theater performed at the Carlton

In terms of meaning, a play like "Wet Paint" is much more meaningful than plays like "Lady Windermere's Fan" or "Melo-Melos." Although at this time of national crisis, in this difficult month of blood and May, it is not enough to shoulder the sacred responsibility of national defense drama.

In "Wet Paint," it ridicules Dr. Ha, the slave of that poor and dirty family. It also illustrates that the works of a so-called "artist" must wait for several years after his death and must pass through the hands of merchants to increase in price and arouse interest. It also sharply points out that there is a kind of so-called critic who, despite pretending to express his noble views, is still always mixed up with merchants and uses each other. Just look at the time when Dr. Ha and Lawson were bargaining, wasn't our noble critic Mr. Dan Wenbo acting as a "fair" appraiser?

Page 20

These are what we can see in the play. Now let's take a step further and see what kind of painter Chrispin, who enjoyed fame fifteen years after his death, was like.

"The Big Stone Bridge" and "The Old Granary," these kinds of landscape paintings, these so-called masterpieces that caused a sensation in London, are actually nothing more than the decadent expressions of the transitional era. These works of art for art's sake happened to suit the temperament of the old men who were going backwards, plus the romance of his "bitter life" before his death. As a result, the entire London was in an uproar. Our noble critic, Mr. Dan Wenbo, wanted to know the detailed romance between Guan Ni and Chrispin. His motive was exactly the same as the motive of the book and painting merchants to collect his posthumous works.

Unfortunately, "Wet Paint" did not expose the ugliness of the noble critic, nor did it explain what kind of painter Chrispin was. It only gave the pitiful and ridiculous family slave—Dr. Ha—a vicious ridicule. Objectively, also because it did not reveal what kind of painter Chrispin was, this artist of art for art's sake also became an artist on the nerves of the audience.

In terms of performance, the director exaggerated the movements of Dr. Ha, which focused the audience's attention on him. That method is very good. However, I think that simply exaggerating the movements of a character will create the danger of disharmony in the entire play. Therefore, I am not against using exaggeration to handle satirical plays, but what is debatable is that each character in the entire play should be given a kind of exaggeration.

As for other things, since the exaggeration method has been used, then in many places, sound effects can be added to further emphasize the exaggerated elements to help with the inadequacy of the movements. (The reason why the impression of the fake inspector eating steak in "The Government Inspector" still remains in our minds is because of this.)

Stage decoration and lighting are the strengths of Zhonglu. In "Wet Paint," the lighting is still well handled, especially the time of each act is well distinguished, so that the audience can tell what time it is at a glance. As for the stage decoration, the composition is not as beautiful as the previous ones. On the wall, after the twelve-pound painting of Ada was taken down, a shadow of the picture frame should be left on the "hard sheet" (this is also mentioned in the lines). But now there is none, which will make the audience lose their sense of reality.

The best of the actors' acting skills is "Dr. Ha" Dai Ya, and the others are almost dimmed by him. (This is related to the special way of exaggerating him.) Zhao Huishen's acting was very hard, but she didn't act very well. Comparatively, Wu Jing's Mrs. Ha was still more harmonious. The rest are all mediocre.

(Scenery of Ya'an, Sichuan) 252

— Recent work by Zhang Shutong

Sending Away the Stupid God (Continued) 253

— Fang Zhou

—Village Customs Collection—

"Help! Are you... are you going to kill me? You... you black-hearted people will not have a good day!..." She just sat in the bamboo basket, shouting, crying, and struggling. But everyone pretended not to hear, and even drank more enthusiastically, running—jumping—bounding—along the stream, by the pond, on the flat ground, on the dangerous slopes, many people forgot their fatigue as if they were crazy, heartlessly playing with this poor woman. The copper gong was also beaten until it made a broken sound, which sounded a bit like Mo Afu's wife's trembling cry!

"Send away the stupid god!" Everyone shouted across the garden.

"Send away the stupid god!" They shouted again across the camphor tree field.

"Mo Afu's wife's stupid god is frightened away!" A group of young people tried their best to shout, until their throats were hoarse, until their clothes were soaked with sweat, but they still had to shout.

They were as excited as if it were a temple fair. When the sun slowly climbed over Qideng Mountain, climbed over Linwu Mountain, and hung high above the Taoist Cave on the top of Silong Mountain, they carried Mo Afu's wife, turned from White Snake Stream to Bandit Mountain, making her almost dead of exhaustion. She fell in the corner of the basket and didn't move, just closing her eyes tightly and letting them do as they pleased, having lost consciousness.

"Throw her in the stream!" Xiao Gen said this to the people carrying the basket.

"The water is too deep, it won't work here," said one of the people carrying the basket.

"The Green Lotus Pond is better, the water is shallower there!"

They passed through the chestnut tree and walked over the Earth Ladder Bridge, arriving at the edge of the Green Lotus Pond.

"Plop!" The woman went into the water together with the basket, and the water splashed very high, wetting many people's bodies.

"Aah!" She managed to call out like this, struggling a few times in the water, and then lay down in the shallow water. Then a few people scrambled down again and fished her out, lying her down on the grass to let her spit out the water she had swallowed.

The sun shone on the old, dirty clothes on her body that were soaked and muddy, her face was terribly pale, her eyeballs were half-staring, her breathing was very rapid and subtle, and her body seemed to be trembling. Someone poked her swollen belly, and a mouthful of water would gurgle out of her mouth.

"Go burn a bowl of reed soup and try to pour it down her!" A Binan said this to his wife. (End)

After the Opening 254

— Zou Heng

The wind has been blowing for two days, and now it has finally stopped. The sun is showing a smiling face, and everything seems to have a bit more vitality. The quiet streets have also become lively right away. However, the most lively place is the health center near the county government—because today is the opening day.

The newly painted gate has two brand-new Kuomintang flags crossed. Next to the gate hangs a wooden plaque with black characters on a white background: "XX County Health Center." The elegant handwriting is immediately recognizable as that of the county magistrate. Inside the gate, all kinds of officials, big and small, from various institutions are crowded together, all in black uniforms and black felt hats. They all have smiling faces, seemingly anticipating the host's social graces. Perhaps because they couldn't find the host, some eyes shifted to the several nurses in white uniforms. Their short, black hair is topped with a snow-white headscarf, which is matched with a white long gown; nestled in this group of black figures, they are distinctly outstanding. It's a pity there are too many people, and the stockings and high heels under their gowns are squeezed and have no chance to be displayed, but even just half of it is enough to be impressive; in this small county town.

Pushing and shoving, they walk through several rooms, look at several smiling faces, and that concludes the tour. Finally, everyone gathers in the auditorium, ready for the official meeting.

With a burst of bell-ringing, a fat man squeezes onto the stage, and a burst of applause erupts below. The fat man squints at the audience, his mouth moving, seemingly speaking, but no one can hear what he is saying. Then they see his mouth stretch into a forced smile, and he comes down. Another round of applause.

After several speeches and rounds of applause, the ceremony concludes. The audience leaves with satisfied smiles, nodding to every smiling face. They elegantly squeeze out of the door. Inside the room, there are still melon seed shells all over the floor.

"Old Li, chase away the idlers outside the door! They're like a wall, surrounding that area. Tell them this isn't a funeral!" The fat man sees off the guests, and as soon as he returns inside the door, he shouts like this.

"Yes." Old Li is busy sweeping up melon seed shells, cigarette butts, and whatnot from the ground, and when he hears this, he drops his broom and runs out. The fat man steps into another room.

"Nurses' Office." A wooden plaque with wet paint hangs beside the door.

"How is it? Satisfied?" Miss Zhang. The fat man returns to his smiling face.

"Terrible! They're all like pigs," Miss Zhang says as she takes off her high heels.

"This is coming to the 'countryside,'" the fat man laughs, then continues, "Of course they're stupid, but that has its advantages: they're easy to deal with." The fat man moves closer to Miss Zhang. The last few words are spoken particularly softly. The response is a burst of giggling laughter.

Movie News

French Teague Lee Thaisak Masterpiece "Escape from Devil's Island" Coming Soon 259

Three small islands on the South American continent, near the Salo Tau Ata Apik Pan Valley (transliteration), are the French-renowned "Devil's Island," the infamous name of the most terrifying and cruel prison solely for incarcerating international and major offenders. Former Captain Terry Fivees was unjustly imprisoned on "Devil's Island" for ten years due to unfounded military conspiracy charges. After his release, a famous French writer wrote a book about his story, which became popular in various countries. Columbia Pictures Corporation has now purchased the rights to adapt it into a film, titled "Escape from Devil's Island," starring the big stars Victor Zorelle, Norman Foster, and the famous actress Florentine Lai. The plot is extremely tense, revealing the suffering of prisoners on the island, showing the inhumane acts of torture and flogging to death. In this film, three prisoners boldly attempt to escape, resulting in shooting and deaths. Although two escape, they are filled with terror and suffer greatly. Simultaneously, love brings about changes, ultimately leading to a resolution where one person willingly sacrifices their own freedom, content to suffer on "Devil's Island," allowing the two lovers to be together. In summary, the value of this film is evident. It is said that the Shanghai Grand Theater has acquired it and will present it to the people of Shanghai in the near future, at which time it will undoubtedly receive high praise from various newspapers.

The Great Miracle of "Peach Blossom Spring Dream": Xu Jia Hui Discovers a Tall Mountain Peak 261

It's been a long time since there's been a comedy film in the domestic film industry. "Peach Blossom Spring Dream" uses the most famous comedy stars on the Chinese silver screen, Han Langen and Liu Jiqun, in the lead roles. This is really great news for movie fans, and what makes everyone even happier is that "Peach Blossom Spring Dream" is showing excellent results. According to those who have seen the unofficial preview of the film, no one can hold back their laughter. These two lively ghosts are active everywhere. Viewers already show a smile when they see their shadows, and they can't help but burst into laughter when they use all their tricks.

During the filming period of "Peach Blossom Spring Dream," Xinhua Company expanded greatly, so it was even more powerful in terms of technical talent. The scenery was designed with Zhang Yunqiao's ingenious psychology. There is a Peach Blossom Spring scene, which covers the twelve acres of Xinhua's new photography studio so tightly that no air can pass through. The entire mountain scene is as high as a three-story Western-style building, so you can already see the mountain peak clearly when you look from the Xu Jia Hui triangle area. Some people were surprised, how can a mountain peak be found in Shanghai? Walking closer and seeing it a mile away, it turns out that it is a large set in the new photography studio of Xinhua Company. This set is already very sensational in the Xu Jia Hui area now, before the film has been released.
